2:29:1521:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:A:ABSTRACT
2:30:1529:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:?:In  this  paper  we  provide  a  model  of  the  macroeconomic  implications  of  safe  asset  shortages.  In 
2:31:1639:14:14:72:546:574:12:Times:12:Times:?:particular, we  discuss  the  emergence  of  a  deflationary  safety  trap  equilibrium  with  endogenous 
2:32:1744:14:14:72:545:560:12:Times:12:Times:?:risk  premia.  It is  an  acute  form  of  a  liquidity  trap,  in  which  the  shortage  of  a  specific  form  of 
2:33:1859:14:14:71:546:546:12:Times:12:Times:?:assets, safe assets, as opposed to a general shortage of assets, is the fundamental driving force. At 
2:34:1960:14:14:71:545:532:12:Times:12:Times:?:the ZLB, our model has a Keynesian cross representation, in which net safe asset supply plays the 
2:35:2057:14:14:72:546:518:12:Times:12:Times:?:role  of  an  aggregate  demand shifter.  Essentially,  safety  traps  correspond  to  liquidity  traps  in 
2:36:2164:14:14:72:545:504:12:Times:12:Times:?:which the emergence of an endogenous risk premium significantly alters the connection between 
2:37:2257:14:14:72:545:490:12:Times:12:Times:?:macroeconomic  policy  and  economic  activity. “Helicopter  drops”  of  money,  safe  public  debt 
2:38:2356:14:14:72:545:476:12:Times:12:Times:?:issuances,  swaps  of  private  risky  assets  for  safe  public debt,  or  increases  in  the  inflation  target, 
2:39:2470:14:14:72:546:462:12:Times:12:Times:?:stimulate aggregate demand and output, while forward guidance is less effective. The safety trap 
2:40:2566:14:14:72:546:448:12:Times:12:Times:?:can  be  arbitrarily  persistent,  as  in  the  secular  stagnation  hypothesis, despite  the  existence  of 
2:41:2674:14:42:72:177:434:12:Times:12:Times:?:infinitely lived assets.

3:59:3018:30:28:287:335:633:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:A:Abstract
3:60:3026:28:17:105:534:605:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f7:?:In this paper we provide a model of the macroeconomic implications of safe asset short-
3:61:3113:17:17:88:534:588:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f7:A:ages. In particular, we discuss the emergence of a deflationarysafety trapequilibrium with
3:62:3203:17:17:88:533:571:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f7:A:endogenous risk premia. It is an acute form of a liquidity trap, in which the shortage of a spe-
3:63:3299:17:17:88:533:554:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f7:A:cific form of assets, safe assets, as opposed to a general shortage of assets, is the fundamental
3:64:3396:17:16:88:533:537:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f7:A:driving force. At the ZLB, our model has a Keynesian cross representation, in which net safe
3:65:3488:16:17:88:533:521:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f7:A:asset supply plays the role of an aggregate demand shifter. Essentially, safety traps correspond
3:66:3584:17:17:88:533:504:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f7:A:to liquidity traps in which the emergence of an endogenous risk premium significantly alters
3:67:3676:17:17:88:533:487:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f7:A:the connection between macroeconomic policy and economic activity. “Helicopter drops” of
3:68:3764:17:17:88:533:470:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f7:A:money, safe public debt issuances, swaps of private risky assets for safe public debt, or increases
3:69:3863:17:16:88:533:453:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f7:A:in the inflation target, stimulate aggregate demand and output, while forward guidance is less
3:70:3957:16:17:88:533:437:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f7:A:effective. The safety trap can be arbitrarily persistent, as in the secular stagnation hypothesis,
3:71:4055:17:35:88:305:420:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f7:A:despite the existence of infinitely lived assets.
3:72:4104:35:36:59:195:385:17:g_d0_f9:17:g_d0_f9:C:1  Introduction
3:73:4119:36:18:59:563:349:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:One of the main structural features of the global economy in recent years is the apparent shortage of
3:74:4220:18:18:59:563:331:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:safe assets. The two black lines in Figure1 illustrate the paths of the short-term interest rate (dark
3:75:4322:18:18:59:563:313:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:blue area) and an estimate of the expected return on equity. The difference between the two lines
3:76:4419:18:18:59:563:295:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:is the equity risk premium (light blue area).1Short-term rates feature a widely noted downward
3:77:4513:18:17:59:563:277:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:secular trend and a sharp drop during the Great Recession. The evolution of the expected return
3:78:4608:17:18:59:563:260:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:on equity is markedly different: It features the same downward trend as the short-term interest
3:79:4703:18:18:59:563:242:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:rate until the early 2000s but then remains more or less stable. The disconnect between a stable
3:80:4799:18:18:59:563:224:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:expected return on equity and a declining short-term interest rate is particularly salient after 2002,
3:81:4901:18:18:59:563:206:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:and even more so since the beginning of the Great Recession. A similar disconnect is observed

4:112:6201:229:14:59:563:500:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Figure 1: Short-term interest rates (one-year Treasury yield), equity risk premium (one-year ahead
4:113:6299:14:15:59:563:486:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:equity risk premium or ERP), and expected return on equity (sum of one-year ahead Treasury yield
4:114:6395:15:14:59:563:471:12:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f7:B:and of one-year ahead ERP).Sources: one-year Treasury yield: Federal Reserve H.15; one year ahead
4:115:6492:14:15:59:563:457:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f7:F:ERP: Duarte and Rosa (2015). The ERP is calculated as the first principal component of twenty models
4:116:6592:15:34:59:265:442:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f7:F:of the one-year-ahead equity risk premium.
4:117:6634:34:17:59:563:408:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:between estimates of real returns on (risky) productive capital by Gomme et al. (2011) as well as
4:118:6731:17:24:59:433:391:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Hall (2014) and short-term interest rates (see e.g. Caballero et al. 2017).
4:119:6806:24:18:77:563:367:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:The stark divergence between safe and risky expected rates of return is suggestive of an increased
4:120:6904:18:18:59:563:349:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:shortage of safe assets, the intensification of which at the onset of the Great Recession pushed the
4:121:7004:18:18:59:563:331:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:U.S. economy against the Zero Lower Bound (ZLB) where it remained for a long time, and still
4:122:7096:18:18:59:563:313:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:remains in many developed economies. Decomposing these developments into shifts in safe asset
4:123:7189:18:18:59:563:295:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:demand and safe asset supply is plagued with difficulties, and some studies attribute the shortage
4:124:7287:18:18:59:563:277:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:to a decrease in the supply of safe assets (see e.g. Barclays 2012 who estimates that about 50% of
4:125:7385:18:18:59:563:259:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the supply of safe assets was destroyed during the U.S. and European crises) while others emphasize
4:126:7484:18:24:59:436:241:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the increase in the demand for safe assets (see e.g. Goldman Sachs 2012).
4:127:7557:24:18:77:563:217:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:In this paper we provide a simple model of the macroeconomic implications of safe asset short-
4:128:7651:18:18:59:563:199:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:ages. Safe assets are in zeronetsupply, issued by some agents to other agents through a process of
4:129:7749:18:18:59:563:181:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:securitization of risky assets in positivenetsupply hampered by a financial friction. We discuss the
4:130:7849:18:17:59:563:163:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:emergence of a deflationarysafety trapequilibrium with endogenous risk premia once the economy
4:131:7943:17:18:59:563:146:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:hits the ZLB. It is an acute form of a liquidity trap, in which the shortage of a specific form of
4:132:8041:18:24:59:549:128:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:assets (safe assets), as opposed to a general shortage of assets, is the fundamental driving force.
4:133:8140:24:18:77:563:104:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:The model is a perpetual youth OLG model with nominal rigidities and heterogeneous agents:
4:134:8230:18:18:59:563:86:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Neutrals (risk neutral) and Knightians (infinitely risk averse). Neutrals act as financial interme-
4:135:8329:18:18:59:563:68:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:diaries by owning risky Lucas’ trees (aggregate risk) and issuing safe assets to Knightians. This
4:136:8426:18:0:59:563:50:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:securitization process is hampered by a financial friction. At a given safe interest rate, as the supply
5:137:8531:0:18:59:563:756:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:of safe assets shrinks relative to demand, a shortage of safe assets develops. The safe interest rate
5:138:8632:18:18:59:563:738:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:drops and the risk premium rises. This mechanism transfers resources from Knightians to Neutrals,
5:139:8729:18:24:59:495:720:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:reduces the demand for safe assets, and restores equilibrium in the safe asset market.
5:140:8815:24:18:77:563:696:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:However, once the safe rate hits the ZLB, the transfer mechanism breaks down, and instead
5:141:8904:18:18:59:563:678:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:equilibrium in the safe asset market is endogenously restored through a drop in output (income),
5:142:9000:18:18:59:563:660:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:which reduces the demand for safe assets. This leads to a dual view of safe asset shortages. As
5:143:9095:18:18:59:563:642:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:long as safe interest rates are positive, safe asset shortages are essentially benign. But when safe
5:144:9195:18:18:59:563:624:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:interest rates reach the ZLB, they become malign. This is because at the ZLB tipping point, the
5:145:9290:18:18:59:563:606:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:virtuous equilibrating mechanism through a reduction in safe interest rates is replaced by a perverse
5:146:9391:18:23:59:345:588:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:equilibrating mechanism through a reduction in output.
5:147:9445:23:18:77:563:565:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:There is an alternative, goods-markets, representation of the equilibrating mechanism. Figure2
5:148:9539:18:18:59:563:547:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:illustrates how equilibrium output (ξX) endogenously drops below exogenous potential output (X)
5:149:9634:18:18:59:563:529:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:at the ZLB (when the safe interest rate isrK= 0). When prices are rigid, the determination of
5:150:9727:18:18:59:563:511:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:equilibrium capacity utilization (ξ) can be represented by a standard Keynesian cross whereAS(ξX)
5:151:9824:18:18:59:563:493:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:is aggregate supply andAD(ξX) is aggregate demand. Reflecting the fact that output is demand
5:152:9916:18:18:59:563:475:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:determined, aggregate supply is simply the 45 degree lineAS(ξX) =ξX. Aggregate demand is
5:153:10004:18:18:59:563:457:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the sum of the aggregate consumptions of Knightians and Neutrals. The aggregate consumption
5:154:10095:18:18:59:563:439:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f16:B:of KnightiansθVSis a constant fractionθof their aggregate wealth which is equal to thegross
5:155:10186:18:18:59:563:421:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:supply of safe assetsVS. The aggregate consumption of Neutrals is equal to their aggregate steady-
5:156:10284:18:18:59:563:403:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:state income which is equal to the sum of their aggregate labor income (1−α)(1−δ)ξXand their
5:157:10376:18:18:59:563:385:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:aggregate dividend incomeδξXnet of the aggregate interest payments to KnightiansrKVS, where
5:158:10467:18:18:59:563:367:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f4:B:δis the fraction of output that accrues as dividends andαis the fraction of Knightians in the
5:159:10560:18:18:59:563:349:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:population (an index of thegrossdemand for safe assets). The key observation is that aggregate
5:160:10654:18:17:59:563:331:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:demand increases with outputξX, decreases with the safe interest raterK, increases with the supply
5:161:10752:17:24:59:410:314:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:of safe assetsVS, decreases with the demand index for safe assetsα.
5:162:10819:24:18:77:562:290:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:Adrop in safe asset supply or an increase in safe asset demand shift aggregate demand down. At
5:163:10913:18:18:59:563:272:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the ZLB, this contractionary demand shock cannot be counteracted by a reduction in safe interest
5:164:11009:18:18:59:563:254:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:ratesrK. The endogenous result is a recession (ξX < X) accompanied by an increase in risk premia
5:165:11105:18:18:59:563:236:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:(r−rK) (determined by the other equilibrium equations of the model). Intuitively, the reduction
5:166:11200:18:18:59:563:218:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:in aggregate demand resulting from a reduction in the supply of safe assets lowers output, which
5:167:11296:18:18:59:563:200:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:further reduces aggregate demand, etc. ad infinitum until the economy reaches a new fixed point
5:168:11391:18:18:59:563:182:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:with lower output. More precisely, the reduction in the value of safe assets reduces the wealth of
5:169:11489:18:18:59:563:164:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Knightians and hence their consumption. This impulse depresses output. This initial reduction in
5:170:11585:18:18:59:563:146:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:output then reduces the income of Neutrals, and hence their consumption, which further reduces
5:171:11679:18:18:59:563:128:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:output. This feedback loop between output and the consumption of Neutrals keeps going until the
5:172:11774:18:18:59:563:110:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:economy settles at a new fixed point with lower values of output, assets, wealth, consumption and
5:173:11871:18:23:59:98:92:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:income.
5:174:11878:23:18:77:563:69:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:When prices have some degree of flexibility captured by a Phillips curve, safety traps trigger de-
5:175:11976:18:0:59:563:51:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:flationary forces, which raise the Keynesian multiplier and exacerbate the output drop by increasing
6:176:12077:0:22:303:338:699:6:g_d0_f19:6:g_d0_f19:?:()
6:177:12079:22:0:302:439:677:6:g_d0_f20:6:g_d0_f20:?:AD(ξX) = (1−α)(1−δ)ξX+δξX+(θ−rK)VS,
6:178:12114:0:137:267:308:714:6:g_d0_f25:6:g_d0_f26:A:AS(ξX) =ξX.
6:179:12125:137:39:380:401:577:6:g_d0_f28:6:g_d0_f28:A:) =ξX.
6:180:12131:39:15:59:563:538:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Figure 2: AS-AD representation and the Keynesian cross. Recession caused by a decrease in the
6:181:12224:15:14:59:563:523:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:supply of safe assets (VS) or an increase in the demand for safe assets (α). Aggregate demand shifts
6:182:12324:14:32:59:89:509:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:down.
6:183:12329:32:24:59:175:477:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:real safe interest rates.
6:184:12354:24:18:77:563:453:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:The safety trap can be arbitrarily persistent, or even permanent, consistent with the secular
6:185:12447:18:18:59:563:435:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:stagnation hypothesis (Hansen 1939, Summers 2013, Eggertsson and Mehrota 2014) and despite
6:186:12537:18:18:59:563:417:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the existence of a positive supply of infinitely lived risky assets (safe assets are in zero net supply):
6:187:12642:18:18:59:563:399:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:The value of risky assets remains finite even when the safe interest rate (rK) is zero because our
6:188:12740:18:18:59:563:381:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:model features risk premia so that the discount rate (r) that applies to the risky cash flows of risky
6:189:12842:18:24:59:256:363:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:infinitely lived assets remains positive.
6:190:12883:24:17:77:563:339:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:Figure2 also hints at the kind of policies that are likely to be effective in a safety trap. Policies
6:191:12984:17:18:59:563:322:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:that increase the gross supply of safe assets (VS), such as “helicopter drops” of money, safe public
6:192:13084:18:18:59:563:304:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:debt issuances, and versions of QE (such as QE1 in the U.S. and LTRO in the Eurozone) involving
6:193:13179:18:18:59:563:286:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:swaps of “positive-beta” private risky assets for “zero-beta” public safe assets, stimulate aggregate
6:194:13280:18:18:59:563:268:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:demand and output, and lower risk premia.2In contrast, Operation Twist (OT) type policies
6:195:13369:18:18:59:563:250:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:involving swaps of “negative-beta” long-term government debt for “zero-beta” short-term public
6:196:13463:18:18:59:563:232:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:debt (such as QE2 and QE3 in the U.S.) are ineffective or even counterproductive.  Similarly,
6:197:13556:18:18:59:563:214:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:policies that seek to stimulate aggregate demand by boosting the value of risky assets, such as
6:198:13651:18:18:59:563:196:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Forward Guidance (FG), are largely ineffective in safety traps because they end up being dissipated
6:199:13750:18:18:59:563:178:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:in higher risk premia: The positive effect of higher future asset values on the current value of
6:200:13846:18:18:59:563:160:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:risky assets is endogenously offset by an increase in risky discount rates (r), limiting the resulting
6:201:13948:18:18:59:563:142:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:increase in wealth and aggregate demand. Finally, policies that succeed in directly reducing the
6:202:14044:18:15:72:563:124:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:F:2We refer the reader to Remark 3 in Section3 and AppendixA.2.3for an analysis of “helicopter drops” of money.
6:203:14153:15:12:59:563:109:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:Their effects depends on whether the extra money is retired using tax revenues once the economy exits the safety
6:204:14265:12:12:59:563:97:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:trap. If it is, then they are equivalent to safe public debt issuances: they generate the same stimulus in the safety
6:205:14382:12:12:59:563:85:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:trap, and they require the same increase in tax revenues after the economy exits the safety trap. If it is not, then
6:206:14498:12:12:59:563:73:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:they are more stimulative than safe public debt issuances, but this extra stimulation is no free lunch and instead
6:207:14612:12:12:59:563:61:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:comes at the cost of an over-stimulation of the economy after the economy exits the safety trap. In both cases,
6:208:14723:12:0:59:228:49:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:money issuances are no “silver bullet”.
7:209:14763:0:18:59:563:756:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:safe real interest rate, such as a large enough and credible increase in the inflation target, lead to
7:210:14865:18:18:59:563:738:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the emergence of a good equilibrium with no recession, positive inflation, and negative safe real
7:211:14962:18:24:59:129:720:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:interest rates.
7:212:14977:24:18:77:563:696:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:The sharp distinction between the risk tolerance of the two groups of agents allows us to isolate
7:213:15074:18:18:59:563:678:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the safety trap from more conventional liquidity traps. In our context, a safety trap corresponds
7:214:15171:18:18:59:563:660:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:to a situation where the economy is at the ZLB and the securitization constraint is binding. In
7:215:15266:18:18:59:563:642:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:contrast, a liquidity trap is a situation where the economy is at the ZLB but the securitization
7:216:15362:18:18:59:563:624:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:constraint isnotbinding. In liquidity traps, in contrast to safety traps, QE does not stimulate
7:217:15457:18:18:59:563:606:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:output while FG does.  Of course reality is not as stark and both type of elements, safety and
7:218:15551:18:17:59:563:588:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:liquidity, are likely to play a role. Our framework is designed to highlight the importance of safe
7:219:15650:17:18:59:563:571:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:asset markets in determining the relative effectiveness of macroeconomic and financial policies in
7:220:15748:18:24:59:135:553:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f10:B:ZLB contexts.3
7:221:15762:24:18:77:563:529:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:We close the paper with a summary of two extensions developed in the appendix: First, the low
7:222:15855:18:18:59:563:511:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:rates of a safety trap environment create a fertile ground for the emergence of bubbles. However, we
7:223:15955:18:18:59:563:493:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:show that risky bubbles do not alleviate the safety trap situation, as they do not expand the stock
7:224:16054:18:18:59:563:475:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:of safe assets.  This formalizes some observations in Summers (2013) that in secular stagnation
7:225:16149:18:18:59:563:457:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:environments, even large financial bubbles only seem to create moderate economic expansions.
7:226:16241:18:18:59:563:439:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Conversely, safe bubbles do alleviate the problem. We associate the latter concept to that of public
7:227:16341:18:18:59:563:421:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:debt, and show that the existence of a bubbly region expands the fiscal capacity of the government
7:228:16439:18:18:59:563:403:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:and reduces the crowding out effect, as bubble-debt does not require future taxation if real rates
7:229:16537:18:18:59:563:385:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:remain secularly low. Second, we show that when the securitization capacity of the economy is
7:230:16630:18:18:59:563:367:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:endogenous, private securitization decisions are efficient outside of a safety trap, but inefficient
7:231:16730:18:18:59:563:349:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:inside of it. This is because in a safety trap, private agents do not internalize the stimulative effects
7:232:16835:18:23:59:447:331:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:of safe asset creation, and hence private incentives to securitize are too low.
7:233:16914:23:18:77:563:308:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:A:Related literature.Our paper is related to several strands of literature.  First and most
7:234:17003:18:18:59:563:290:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:closely related is the literature that identifies the shortage of safe assets as a key macroeconomic
7:235:17103:18:18:59:563:272:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:fact (see e.g.  Caballero 2006, Caballero et al.  2008a and 2008b, Caballero and Krishnamurthy
7:236:17197:18:18:59:563:254:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:2009, Caballero 2010, Bernanke et al. 2011, and Barclay’s 2012).4Our paper provides a model
7:237:17288:18:17:59:563:236:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:that captures many of the key insights in that literature and that allows us to study the main
7:238:17382:17:16:72:563:219:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:F:3For example, the complete ineffectiveness of FG in safety traps as opposed to standard liquidity traps is an
7:239:17491:16:12:59:563:203:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:extreme result, which relies on the stark assumptions of the model. It should not be interpreted as an indictment
7:240:17604:12:12:59:563:191:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:of FG, but rather as a demonstration that the features of safety traps, even if they appear only in some milder
7:241:17715:12:12:59:563:179:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:forms, are likely to mitigate the effect of FG. In this sense, the safety trap offers a possible resolution of the “forward
7:242:17838:12:12:59:563:167:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:guidance puzzle”, a term that refers to the discrepancy between the implausibly large effects of forward guidance
7:243:17951:12:12:59:563:155:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:in standard New Keynesian DSGE models of liquidity traps and its more limited effects observed in the data. See
7:244:18062:12:12:59:563:143:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:e.g. Carlstrom et al. (2012) and Del Negro et al. (2015) for an exposition of this puzzle. See also Del Negro et al.
7:245:18178:12:12:59:563:131:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:(2015) and McKay et al. (2015) for other possible rationalizations in models with incomplete markets and borrowing
7:246:18292:12:8:59:109:119:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:constraints.
7:247:18304:8:15:72:563:111:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:F:4Caballero et al. (2008a,b) developed the idea that global imbalances originated in the superior development
7:248:18412:15:12:59:563:96:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:of financial markets in developed economies, and in particular the U.S. Global imbalances resulted from an asset
7:249:18524:12:12:59:563:84:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:imbalance. Although we do not develop the open economy version of our model here (see Caballero et al. 2015), our
7:250:18637:12:12:59:563:72:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:model could capture a specific channel that lies behind global imbalances: The latter were caused by the funding
7:251:18749:12:12:59:563:60:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:countries’ demand for financial assets in excess of their ability to produce them, but this gap is particularly acute
7:252:18866:12:0:59:483:48:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:for safe assets since emerging markets have very limited institutional capability to produce them.
8:253:18965:0:18:59:563:756:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:macroeconomic policy implications of this environment more precisely. Like us, Barro and Mollerus
8:254:19062:18:18:59:563:738:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:(2014) considers an environment with heterogenous risk aversion. They show that such a model can
8:255:19158:18:18:59:563:720:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:quantitatively match the value of safe assets to GDP as well as a number of asset pricing facts. He
8:256:19257:18:18:59:563:702:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:et al. (2015) emphasize that the public supply of safe assets is determined not only by fiscal capacity
8:257:19360:18:18:59:563:684:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:(as in our paper), but also by self-fulfilling expectations supported by strategic complementarities
8:258:19460:18:24:59:365:666:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:among investors arising in the presence of default decisions.
8:259:19521:24:18:77:563:642:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:Second, there is the literature on liquidity traps (see e.g. Keynes 1936, Krugman 1998, Eggerts-
8:260:19617:18:18:59:563:624:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:son and Woodford 2003, Christiano, Eichenbaum and Rebelo 2011, Correia et al. 2012, and Werning
8:261:19712:18:18:59:563:606:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:2012). This literature emphasizes that the binding ZLB on nominal interest rates presents a chal-
8:262:19809:18:17:59:563:588:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:lenge for macroeconomic stabilization. Recent models (see e.g. Guerrieri and Lorenzoni 2011, and
8:263:19905:17:18:59:563:571:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Eggertsson and Krugman 2012) emphasize the role of tightened borrowing constraints in economies
8:264:20000:18:18:59:563:553:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:with heterogeneous agents (borrowers and savers) in generating the aggregate demand contraction
8:265:20095:18:18:59:563:535:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:that brings the economy into the ZLB. In our model it is the shortage of safe assets that causes a
8:266:20193:18:24:59:352:517:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:similar phenomenon, with distinctive policy implications.
8:267:20250:24:18:77:563:493:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:Third, there is an emerging literature on secular stagnation: the possibility of a permanent ZLB
8:268:20346:18:18:59:563:475:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:situation (see e.g. Kocherlakota 2013 and especially Eggertsson and Mehrota 2014). Like us, they
8:269:20442:18:18:59:563:457:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:use an OLG structure with a ZLB. Unlike us, they do not consider risk and risk premia. As we show,
8:270:20540:18:18:59:563:439:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:this difference has important consequences for the relative effectiveness of different policy options.
8:271:20642:18:18:59:563:421:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:An additional difference has to do with the theoretical possibility of permanent ZLB equilibrium in
8:272:20741:18:18:59:563:403:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the presence of infinitely-lived assets, such as land. Indeed, infinitely-lived assets would rule out a
8:273:20844:18:18:59:563:385:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:permanent ZLB in Kocherlakota (2013) and Eggertsson and Mehrota (2014). In our model, trees
8:274:20935:18:18:59:563:367:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:are infinitely lived but their value remains finite even when the safe interest rate is permanently at
8:275:21037:18:18:59:563:349:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:zero. This is only possible because our model features risk and risk premia, which are ignored in
8:276:21134:18:17:59:563:331:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:most liquidity trap analyzes. Finally, our modelling of inflation in Section5 borrows heavily from
8:277:21232:17:24:59:224:314:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Eggertsson and Mehrota (2014).
8:278:21262:24:18:77:563:290:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:Fourth, there is a literature that documents significant deviations from the predictions of stan-
8:279:21359:18:18:59:563:272:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:dard asset-pricing models—patterns which can be thought of as reflecting money-like convenience
8:280:21454:18:18:59:563:254:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:services—in the pricing of Treasury securities generally, and in the pricing of short-term T-bills
8:281:21552:18:18:59:563:236:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:more specifically (Krishnamurthy and Vissing-Jorgensen 2011, 2012, Greenwood and Vayanos 2010,
8:282:21646:18:18:59:563:218:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Duffee 1996, Gurkaynak et al. 2006). Our model offers an interpretation of these stylized facts,
8:283:21742:18:24:59:466:200:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:where the “specialness” of public debt is its safety during bad aggregate states.
8:284:21823:24:18:77:563:176:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:Fifth, there is a literature which emphasizes how the aforementioned premium creates incentives
8:285:21918:18:18:59:563:158:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:for private agents to rely heavily on short-term debt, even when this creates systemic instabilities
8:286:22018:18:18:59:563:140:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:(Gorton 2010, Stein 2012, Woodford 2012, Gennaioli et al.  2012).  Greenwood et al.  (2012)
8:287:22109:18:18:59:563:122:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:consider the role of the government in increasing the supply of short-term debt and affecting the
8:288:22206:18:18:59:563:104:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:premium. Gorton and Ordonez (2013) also consider this question but in the context of a model with
8:289:22303:18:17:59:563:86:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:(asymmetric) information acquisition about collateral where the key characteristic of public debt
8:290:22400:17:18:59:563:69:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:that drives its premium is its information insensitivity. The inefficiency takes the form of too much
8:291:22501:18:0:59:563:51:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:securitization. It occurs ex ante (before the crisis), because of a pecuniary externality (fire sales).
9:292:22605:0:18:59:563:756:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Instead, in our model, the inefficiency takes the form of too little securitization. The inefficiency
9:293:22706:18:18:59:563:738:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:occurs ex post (during the crisis) if there is a safety trap, and it does not originate in a pecuniary
9:294:22808:18:24:59:563:720:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:externality, but rather in a Keynesian externality operating through the level of aggregate demand.
9:295:22907:24:18:77:563:696:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:The paper is organized as follows. Section2 describes our basic model and introduces the key
9:296:22999:18:18:59:563:678:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:mechanism of a safety trap. Section3 introduces public debt and considers the effects of QE policies.
9:297:23100:18:18:59:563:660:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Section4 analyzes the role of forward guidance. Section5 introduces inflation. Section6 discusses
9:298:23197:18:18:59:563:642:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the robustness of the results to a relaxation of some of the extreme assumptions of the model. It
9:299:23294:18:18:59:563:624:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:also summarizes two extensions discussed in the Appendix: the emergence and role of bubbles, and
9:300:23390:18:18:59:563:606:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the presence of a securitization externality. Section7 concludes and is followed by an extensive
9:301:23486:18:51:59:109:588:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:appendix.
9:302:23495:51:35:59:181:537:17:g_d0_f9:17:g_d0_f9:C:2  The Model
9:303:23507:35:18:59:563:502:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:In this section we introduce our basic model, which is a stylized stochastic overlapping generations
9:304:23607:18:18:59:563:484:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:model.  We start by developing a benchmark flexible price model.  We then introduce nominal
9:305:23698:18:18:59:563:466:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:rigidities, whose only purpose is to bring relevance to the nominal ZLB. In this model, as long as
9:306:23796:18:18:59:563:448:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:safe nominal interest rates are positive, safe assets shortages can be accommodated with reductions
9:307:23895:18:18:59:563:430:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:in safe nominal interest rates. The associated reduction in the return of safe assets reduces their
9:308:23994:18:18:59:563:412:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:demand and restores equilibrium in the market for safe assets. But if safe nominal interest rates
9:309:24091:18:45:59:540:394:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:are at the ZLB, then a safety trap emerges and asset markets are cleared through a recession.
9:310:24184:45:32:59:285:349:14:g_d0_f9:14:g_d0_f9:C:2.1  Flexible Prices Benchmark
9:311:24214:32:18:59:563:317:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:B:Demographics.The horizon is infinite and time is continuous. Population is constant and nor-
9:312:24306:18:17:59:563:299:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:malized to one. Agents are born and die at hazard rateθ, independent across agents. Each dying
9:313:24400:17:18:59:563:282:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f17:B:agent is instantaneously replaced by a newborn. Therefore, in an intervaldt,θdtagents die andθdt
9:314:24496:18:24:59:142:264:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:agents are born.
9:315:24512:24:18:77:563:240:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:A:Aggregate risk.We model aggregate risk as follows. There are twoaggregatePoisson processes:
9:316:24603:18:18:59:563:222:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:a good Poisson process with intensityλ+and a bad Poisson process with intensityλ−. We denote
9:317:24695:18:18:59:563:204:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:byσ+andσ−the stopping times for the realizations of the good and bad Poisson processes. We
9:318:24785:18:18:59:563:186:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:define a Poisson event to be the first realization of either the good or the bad Poisson process, with
9:319:24887:18:18:59:563:168:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f10:B:corresponding stopping timeσ= min{σ+, σ−}.   We say that the Poisson event is good ifσ=σ+
9:320:24976:18:18:59:563:150:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:and bad ifσ=σ−. Before the Poisson event, fort< σ, outputXtper unit of time is equal toX.
9:321:25065:18:18:59:563:132:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:After the Poisson event, fort≥σ, outputXtis equal to-+X > Xif the Poisson event is good,
9:322:25153:18:18:59:563:114:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f16:B:and to-−X < Xif the Poisson event is bad. The focus of our analysis is on the periodbefore
9:323:25243:18:18:59:563:96:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the realization of the aggregate Poisson event, when agents make portfolio decisions in anticipation
9:324:25343:18:18:59:563:78:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:of such an event. While most of our results only rely on the bad Poisson event, the good Poisson
9:325:25439:18:0:59:563:60:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:event will be important when we consider the effects of forward guidance, and so we introduce it
10:326:25536:0:24:59:134:756:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:from the start.
10:327:25551:24:18:77:563:732:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:A:Preferences.We assume that agents only have an opportunity to consume when they die,
10:328:25635:18:18:59:563:714:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f4:B:ct. We denote byσθthe stopping time for the idiosyncratic Poisson process controlling an agent’s
10:329:25731:18:18:59:563:696:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:death. This risk is uninsurable and plays no role in our model, aside from its aggregate saving
10:330:25826:18:24:59:119:678:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:implication.
10:331:25838:24:18:77:563:654:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:There are two types of agents in the population: a fractionαof Knightians and 1−αof Neutrals,
10:332:25931:18:18:59:563:636:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:with identical demographics. These agents have different preferences over aggregate risk: Knightians
10:333:26031:18:18:59:563:618:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:are infinitely risk averse over short time intervals, while Neutrals are risk neutrals over short time
10:334:26133:18:18:59:563:600:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:intervals. More precisely, for a given stochastic consumption process{ct}w   hich is measurable with
10:335:26233:18:17:59:563:582:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f17:B:respect to the information available at datet, we define the utilityUNtof a Neutral alive at datet,
10:336:26332:17:33:59:517:565:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:andUKtof a Knightian alive at datet,with the following stochastic differential equations
10:337:26420:33:33:214:408:532:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f17:A:UNt= 1{t−dt≤σθ<t}ct+ 1{t≤σθ}Et[UNt+dt],

10:342:26700:18:24:59:218:419:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:information available at datet.
10:343:26731:24:18:77:563:395:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:Note that the information at datetcontains the information about the realization of the id-
10:344:26822:18:17:59:563:377:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:iosyncratic and aggregate Poisson events up tot, implying that 1{t−dt≤σθ<t}andctare known at
10:345:26914:17:18:59:563:360:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:datet. Similarly, the conditional expectationEtis an expectation over both aggregate shocks and
10:346:27009:18:24:59:238:342:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:idiosyncratic Poisson death shocks.
10:347:27044:24:18:77:563:318:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:Basically, Neutrals are risk neutral with no discounting, and Knightians have Epstein-Zin pref-
10:348:27139:18:18:59:563:300:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:erences with infinite relative risk aversion and infinite intertemporal elasticity of substitution, with
10:349:27243:18:18:59:563:282:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:no discounting. When there is no aggregate risk (as happens after an aggregate Poisson event), the
10:350:27341:18:24:59:306:264:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:preferences of Knightians and Neutrals coincide.
10:351:27389:24:18:77:563:240:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:A:Non-traded inputs, monopolistic competition, and output.Even though we assume
10:352:27466:18:18:59:572:222:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:that prices are flexible in this section, we will later introduce nominal rigidities in Section2.2  .
10:353:27567:18:18:59:563:204:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:To be able to do so, we introduce monopolistic competition: We assume that monopolistic firms
10:354:27660:18:18:59:563:186:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:produce imperfectly substitutable varieties of final goods and compete in prices. Later, when we

10:356:27854:18:18:59:563:150:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:accommodate demand at the posted price. These are standard modelling assumptions in the New
10:357:27945:18:23:59:378:132:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Keynesian literature following Blanchard and Kiyotaki (1987).

11:413:30559:18:18:59:563:260:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:state-contingent securities to outside investors (other Neutrals or Knightians) against the cash
11:414:30655:18:18:59:563:242:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:flows of that tree. We assume that these state-contingent securities cannot be made contingent on
11:415:30752:18:18:59:563:224:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:idiosyncratic death Poisson processes. Neutrals therefore act like banks in many models of financial
11:416:30852:18:24:59:333:206:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:intermediation (see e.g. Holmstr ̈om and Tirole 1997).
11:417:30906:24:18:77:563:182:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:The securitization process is hampered by an agency problem: only a fractionρof the cash flows
11:418:31000:18:18:59:563:164:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:of each tree can be pledged to outside investors. This assumption could be motivated in various
11:419:31095:18:18:59:563:146:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:ways. One popular microfoundation in the financial constraints literature (see e.g. Holmstr ̈om and
11:420:31194:18:18:59:563:128:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Tirole 1997, 1998, Kiyotaki and Moore 1997, and a vast literature since then) is the existence of a
11:421:31293:18:18:59:564:110:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:moral hazard problem whereby the owner of a tree can abscond with a fraction 1−ρof the cash
11:422:31384:18:23:59:398:92:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:flows. We refer toρas thesecuritization capacityof the economy.
11:423:31447:23:18:77:563:69:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:We also make two technical financial friction assumptions which we maintain throughout the
11:424:31537:18:0:59:563:51:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:paper. The first assumption,ρ > α, ensures that the financial friction would have no bite in the
12:425:31634:0:18:59:563:756:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:absence of aggregate risk (i.e., if we had-+=-−= 1). This allows us to isolate the limits to the

17:699:46270:37:18:59:563:665:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f30:F:Remark 2Our model features two forms of market incompleteness.  The first one is tied to our
17:700:46362:18:18:59:563:647:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:overlapping generations structure, which makes future endowment (“wages”) non-pledgeable.  The
17:701:46456:18:18:59:563:629:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:second market incompleteness is the pledegeability of dividends constraint (ρ) which limits the ability
17:702:46559:18:18:59:563:611:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:to securitize (tranche) Lucas’ trees.  Tranching is desirable because it decomposes an asset into a
17:703:46658:18:17:59:563:593:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:safe tranche which can be sold to Knightian agents and a risky tranche. In the policy discussion we
17:704:46757:17:18:59:563:576:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:will not exploit the first form of incompleteness (we use the OLG structure mostly because it yields a
17:705:46859:18:18:59:563:558:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:stationary distribution of wealth between Neutrals and Knightians) and focus instead on the second
17:706:46957:18:18:59:563:540:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:form.  The latter implies that in equilibrium risky assets held by Neutrals contain an unpledgable
17:707:47055:18:18:59:563:522:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:safe claim of size(1−ρ)-−Xθwhich is the starting point of our macroeconomic policy analysis later
17:708:47152:18:45:59:308:504:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:C:on.See Section3 for a more detailed discussion.

17:714:47658:18:17:59:563:355:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:output, we also sometimes use the term potential output. It is equal toXbefore the Poisson event,
17:715:47755:17:24:59:443:338:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:to-+Xa   fter a good Poisson event, and to-−Xa   fter a bad Poisson event.
17:716:47829:24:18:77:563:314:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:With nominal rigidities, there is potentially a gap betweenactual outputandpotential output.
17:717:47921:18:18:59:563:296:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Appropriate monetary policy can ensure that actual output is at potential as long as the safe natural
17:718:48022:18:18:59:563:278:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:interest rate is positive. But when the safe natural interest rate is negative, the economy reaches
17:719:48121:18:24:59:316:260:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the ZLB and actual output drops below potential.
17:720:48169:24:18:77:563:236:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:Depending on whether we are in the unconstrained regime where the financial friction is slack
17:721:48262:18:18:59:563:218:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:and the heterogeneity in risk aversion plays no role, or in the constrained regime where it is binding
17:722:48364:18:18:59:563:200:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f16:B:and where the heterogeneity in risk aversion matters, the situation that emerges is either aliquidity
17:723:48465:18:18:59:563:182:12:g_d0_f16:12:g_d0_f4:B:trapor asafety  trap.In our rendition, liquidity traps feature no risk premia while safety traps
17:724:48561:18:18:59:563:164:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:feature positive and endogenous risk premia.  It will become apparent that the key distinction
17:725:48655:18:18:59:563:146:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:between the two situations has to do with the difference in the sensitivity of risk premia and its
17:726:48753:18:23:59:142:128:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f10:B:specific drivers.9
17:727:48771:23:18:77:563:105:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:Our focus is on the safety trap, which is novel, but we also characterize the more standard
17:728:48862:18:19:59:563:87:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:liquidity trap as it will help us to highlight (by contrast) the unique policy implications of safety
17:729:48963:19:15:72:563:68:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:F:9In the broader literature on liquidity traps, risk premia are either assumed away by analysis relying on log-
17:730:49073:15:0:59:433:53:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:linearizations or play at best a peripheral role in analyses with non-linearized models.
18:731:49163:0:41:59:182:756:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:traps later in the paper.
18:732:49188:41:31:59:361:715:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:C:2.2.1  Rigid Prices, Monetary Policy, and the ZLB
18:733:49237:31:18:59:563:684:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:We use the traditional ingredients of New Keynesian economics: imperfect competition, sticky
18:734:49329:18:24:59:230:666:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:prices, and a monetary authority.
18:735:49362:24:18:77:563:642:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:A:Rigid prices.We assume that the prices of the different varieties are entirely fixed (an extreme
18:736:49458:18:18:59:563:624:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:form of sticky prices, which we shall relax later in Section5) and equal to each other,pi t=P,
18:737:49552:18:18:59:563:606:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:where without loss of generality we takeP= 1. Monopolistic firms accommodate demand for their
18:738:49645:18:24:59:266:588:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:variety of final good at the posted price.
18:739:49687:24:18:77:563:564:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:Because the prices of all varieties are identical, the demand for all varieties is the same. Output

20:838:54687:24:17:77:563:513:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:The first part of the mechanism is as follows. The economy undergoes an immediate wealth
20:839:54775:17:18:59:563:496:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:adjustment (the wealth of Knightians drops) through a round of trading between Knightians and
20:840:54868:18:18:59:563:478:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Neutrals born in previous periods. At impact, Knightians hold assets that now carry some risk.
20:841:54962:18:18:59:563:460:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:They react by selling the risky part of their portfolio to Neutrals. This shedding of risky assets
20:842:55060:18:18:59:563:442:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:catalyzes an instantaneous fire sale whereby the price of risky assets collapses before immediately
20:843:55159:18:18:59:563:424:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:recovering once risky assets have changed hands. Needless to say, in reality this phase takes time,
20:844:55258:18:24:59:441:406:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:which we have removed to focus on the phase following the initial turmoil.

20:847:55513:18:18:59:563:346:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:takes place.  This reduction in the safe interest rate effectively implements a transfer (in every
20:848:55611:18:18:59:563:328:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:period) from Knightians to Neutrals, which limits the growth of Knightian wealth. As a result, the
20:849:55709:18:18:59:563:310:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:safe asset market remains in equilibrium, and so does the goods market. But if the safe interest rate
20:850:55810:18:18:59:563:292:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:is against the ZLBrK=i=0, then this reduction in the safe interest rate cannot take place and

20:852:55998:18:23:59:317:256:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:(income), which also drags down Neutral’s wealth.

23:1010:63843:18:18:59:563:397:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:whenrn=rK,n<0   , andr=rK=i=0, at full employment, there is an excess demand for assets.
23:1011:63931:18:18:59:563:379:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:It is easy to see that a recession reduces asset demand more than asset supply, and lowers the excess
23:1012:64032:18:24:59:532:361:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:demand for assets, and helps restore equilibrium (otherwise, there is simply no equilibrium).
23:1013:64125:24:18:77:563:337:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:A:AS-AD representation and the Keynesian cross.We can also provide an AS-AD Keyne-

23:1031:64872:18:30:59:251:93:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:demand and aggregate supply curves.
23:1032:64907:30:0:77:563:63:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:A:Safety traps vs.  liquidity traps.We conclude this section by highlighting three broad
24:1033:64995:0:37:59:293:756:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:differences between safety and liquidity traps:
24:1034:65042:37:18:76:563:719:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:A:•Risk premium.Both safety traps and liquidity traps occur when the natural safe interest rate
24:1035:65135:18:18:88:563:701:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:is negativerK,n<0    and the ZLB bindsi=rK= 0. In both cases a recession ensuesξ<1. The
24:1036:65222:18:18:88:563:683:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:key difference between safety traps and liquidity traps is the reason behind the ZLB: Safety
24:1037:65314:18:18:88:563:665:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:traps arise because of a shortage of safe assets and positive while liquidity traps originate in
24:1038:65410:18:18:88:563:647:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:a shortage of assets in general. Positive and endogenous risk premia are at the core of the
24:1039:65501:18:18:88:563:629:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:mechanics of safety traps, while they only play a peripheral role in liquidity traps (in fact, in
24:1040:65598:18:18:88:563:611:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:our rendition, they are zero). The securitization capacityρ, and more generally the supply of
24:1041:65691:18:17:88:563:593:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:safe assetsVSplay no role in liquidity traps, whereas they are the key bottlenecks in safety
24:1042:65783:17:18:88:563:576:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:traps. Aside from the direct relevance of endogenous risk premia during severe recessions,
24:1043:65873:18:18:88:563:558:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:this distinction has important implications for the persistence and policy implications of the
24:1044:65967:18:28:88:208:540:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:different kinds of traps.
24:1045:65992:28:18:76:563:512:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:A:•Persistence and secular stagnation.The possibility of a permanent ZLB equilibrium is some-
24:1046:66083:18:18:88:563:494:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:times disputed on the grounds that this would imply an infinite value for infinitely-lived
24:1047:66173:18:18:88:563:476:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:assets, such as land. In our model, Lucas trees are indeed infinitely lived, and for that reason,
24:1048:66270:18:18:88:563:458:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:a permanent liquidity trap cannot occur. Indeed, in the limitλ+→0andλ−→0    , we have
24:1049:66355:18:18:88:563:440:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f4:A:rK,n=δθ >0 so that a liquidity trap is simply impossible. In contrast, in the constrained
24:1050:66444:18:0:88:456:422:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f18:A:regime, in the limitλ+→0andλ−→0    , we haverK,n=δθ−α−ρ-
24:1051:66500:0:12:456:462:430:6:g_d0_f35:6:g_d0_f35:?:−
24:1052:66501:12:14:440:563:418:8:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f4:A:ρ-−(1−δ)θwhich can
24:1053:66519:14:18:88:563:404:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:be negative. In that case, an essentially permanent safety trap emerges. The value of trees
24:1054:66610:18:18:88:563:386:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:remains finite even when the safe interest rate isrK=i=0 because our model features risk
24:1055:66698:18:18:88:563:368:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:premia so that the discount rate that applies to the risky cash flows of Lucas trees remains
24:1056:66790:18:27:88:162:350:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:positiver >0.
24:1057:66803:27:18:76:563:323:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f4:A:•Policy options:  a roadmap.In the next sections, we analyze policy options in safety traps,
24:1058:66895:18:18:88:563:305:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:and contrast them briefly with liquidity traps. In safety traps, effective stimulative policies
24:1059:66990:18:18:88:563:287:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:work by influencing the value of safe assetsVS(public debt issuances and QE in Section3)
24:1060:67078:18:23:88:357:269:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:andrK(increasing the inflation target in Section5).
24:1061:67129:23:18:88:563:246:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:The risky raterdoesnotappear either in aggregate demand or in aggregate supply. The
24:1062:67212:18:0:88:285:228:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:equilibrium is block-recursive inξand
24:1063:67249:0:10:289:294:238:12:g_d0_f34:12:g_d0_f34:A:(
24:1064:67250:10:0:294:320:228:12:g_d0_f17:8:g_d0_f18:?:r, VR
24:1065:67255:0:10:321:326:238:12:g_d0_f34:12:g_d0_f34:?:)
24:1066:67256:10:18:326:563:228:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:.Even whenλ+>0   , the future value of risky
24:1067:67300:18:18:88:563:210:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:assets after the good Poisson event does not affect the determination ofξ(it only matters
24:1068:67389:18:18:88:563:192:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:for the risky rate of returnrand the risk premiumr−rK). This point will prove crucial
24:1069:67474:18:18:88:563:174:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:later on when we discuss theineffectivenessof forward guidance in a safety trap (Section
24:1070:67562:18:18:88:563:156:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:4).  In sharp contrast, the relative effectiveness of safe public debt issuances and QE and
24:1071:67653:18:18:88:563:138:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:the relative ineffectiveness of Forward Guidance (FG) in safety traps are exactly inverted in
24:1072:67746:18:18:88:563:120:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:liquidity traps. Public debt issuances and QE become ineffective because they increase the
24:1073:67836:18:18:88:563:102:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:value of safe assetsVSbut crowd out the value of risky assetsVRand hence do not increase
24:1074:67924:18:17:88:563:84:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:the value of assetsVin general. FG becomes effective in liquidity traps because whenλ+>0   ,
24:1075:68016:17:0:88:552:67:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:the future value of risky assets after the good Poisson event affects the determination ofξ.
25:1076:68110:0:18:77:563:756:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:In the rest of the paper, we focus on the constrained regime and safety traps in the main text,
25:1077:68205:18:51:59:536:738:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:and treat the unconstrained regime and liquidity traps in remarks at the end of each section.
25:1078:68298:51:36:59:403:687:17:g_d0_f9:17:g_d0_f9:C:3  Public Debt and Quantitative Easing
25:1079:68336:36:18:59:563:651:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:In this section we introduce safe public debt to our analysis. We focus on the safety creation and
25:1080:68434:18:18:59:563:633:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:transformation roles of the government by assuming that the taxes that support public debt are
25:1081:68528:18:18:59:563:615:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:levied on dividends (and are hence fully capitalized). As a result, the economy is de facto Ricardian
25:1082:68629:18:24:59:369:597:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:in the unconstrained regime, but not in the constrained one.
25:1083:68689:24:18:77:563:573:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:The government’s capacity to increase the total supply of safe assets by issuing safe public debt
25:1084:68786:18:18:59:563:555:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:depends on two factors:fiscal capacityandcrowding out of private safe assets by public safe assets.
25:1085:68885:18:18:59:563:537:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:In a safe asset shortage situation, the relevant form of fiscal capacity is the government’s ability to
25:1086:68988:18:17:59:563:519:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:raise taxes in the bad events feared by Knightians. Crowding out, on the other hand, depends on
25:1087:69083:17:18:59:563:502:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:how much these taxes reduce the private sector’s capacity to issue safe claims backed by the risky
25:1088:69181:18:18:59:563:484:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:dividends of Lucas trees. In our model, there is less crowding out when the securitization capacity
25:1089:69280:18:18:59:563:466:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:of the economy is impaired (when the financial friction is severe). In a safety trap, issuing public
25:1090:69380:18:18:59:563:448:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:debt, and possibly undertaking QE by purchasing private risky assets, increases the supply of safe
25:1091:69478:18:18:59:563:430:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:assets, stimulates the economy, and reduces risk premia. By contrast, these policies are much less
25:1092:69576:18:45:59:433:412:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:relevant (irrelevant in our stylized model) in conventional liquidity traps.
25:1093:69652:45:32:59:326:367:14:g_d0_f9:14:g_d0_f9:C:3.1  Public Debt and Fiscal Capacity
25:1094:69688:32:24:59:522:335:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:B:Public debt.Let us first introduce safe public debt outside of a safety trap withrK>0   .
25:1095:69777:24:18:77:563:311:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:The government taxes dividends,δX. The tax rate isτ+after the good Poisson event occurs,

25:1097:69964:17:18:59:563:276:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f4:B:τtthat satisfies the government flow budget constraint. The government issues a fixed amount of
25:1098:70059:18:18:59:563:258:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:risk-free bonds that capitalize future tax revenues and pays a variable raterKt. The proceeds of the
25:1099:70159:18:24:59:381:240:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:sales of these bonds are rebated lump-sum to agents at date 0.

25:1105:70287:37:18:59:563:144:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f30:F:Assumption 1(Regalian taxation power):  Taxes backing government safe debt can be levied on
25:1106:70378:18:37:59:440:126:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:C:the claim(1−ρ)-−Xθto the privately unpledgable part of future dividends.
25:1107:70450:37:18:77:563:89:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:That is, the government is essentially better than private investors at collecting dividend rev-
25:1108:70546:18:18:59:563:71:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:enues from Neutrals once borrowers’ incentives are weak, and can hence essentially get around the

26:1115:71158:24:18:77:563:660:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:Note, however, that the scope for policy depends crucially on the securitization capacity of the

26:1148:72849:23:16:69:563:211:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:F:16This mechanism has some commonality with the idea in Holmstr ̈om and Tirole (1998) that the government has
26:1149:72957:16:11:59:563:195:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:a comparative advantage in providing liquidity. In their model like in ours, this result arises from the assumption
26:1150:73072:11:12:59:563:184:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:that some agents (consumers in their model) lack commitment and hence cannot borrow because they cannot issue
26:1151:73181:12:12:59:563:172:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:securities that pledge their future endowments. This can result in a scarcity of stores of value. The government can
26:1152:73297:12:12:59:563:160:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:alleviate this scarcity by issuing public debt and repaying this debt by taxing consumers. The proceeds of the debt
26:1153:73412:12:12:59:563:148:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:issuance can actually be rebated to consumers. At the aggregate level, this essentially relaxes the borrowing constraint
26:1154:73532:12:12:59:563:136:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:of consumers, as they borrow indirectly through the government.  In their model like in ours, the comparative
26:1155:73641:12:12:59:563:124:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:advantage of the government in providing liquidity arises because it is better than private lenders at collecting
26:1156:73754:12:9:59:170:112:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:revenues from consumers.
26:1157:73778:9:15:69:563:103:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:F:17We assume throughout that the technical financial friction assumptions as well as condition (1) hold whenρis

28:1264:76624:0:18:59:563:756:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:The stimulative effects of safe public debt can be understood most clearly by going back to our
28:1265:76719:18:18:59:563:738:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:AS-AD equilibrium representation. Because issuing safe public debt increases the supply of safe
28:1266:76814:18:18:59:563:720:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:assetsVS, it produces and upward shift in aggregate demand, which in turn results in a proportional
28:1267:76913:18:24:59:349:702:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f10:B:increase in output through the Keynesian multiplier.21,22
28:1268:76970:24:18:77:563:678:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:In the model, we necessarily haveτ+-+=τ−-−, which implies thatτ+< τ−. For this reason, it
28:1269:77059:18:18:59:563:660:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:is natural to expect fiscal constraints to be more binding after the bad Poisson event than after the
28:1270:77160:18:18:59:563:642:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:good Poisson event. This is why we adoptτ−, a measure of the ability of the government to raise
28:1271:77255:18:18:59:563:624:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:tax revenues after the bad Poisson event, as our measure offuture fiscal capacity. In particular, in
28:1272:77355:18:18:59:563:606:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f16:B:a safety trap, increasing the supply of safe public debt toˆDrequires the government to havespare
28:1273:77452:18:37:59:549:588:12:g_d0_f16:12:g_d0_f4:B:future fiscal capacity; that is to have the ability to raise more taxes after the bad Poisson event
28:1274:77551:37:0:268:293:551:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:ˆτ−=
28:1275:77555:0:19:300:308:562:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f17:?:ˆD

28:1278:77565:33:18:59:563:518:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Note however that taxes do not have to be raised while the economy is in the safety trap before
28:1279:77660:18:18:59:563:500:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the Poisson event. Indeed ˆτ=τ(and both are equal to 0) since the safe interest rates on debt is
28:1280:77756:18:24:59:98:482:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f4:B:rK= 0.
28:1281:77762:24:18:77:563:458:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:If the government issues more public debt than can be supported by its future fiscal capacity,
28:1282:77856:18:17:59:563:440:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:then public debt becomes risky. For example, suppose thatτ−has an upped bound at  ̄τ−reached
28:1283:77948:17:15:59:563:423:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:for a level of public debt ̄Dsuch that  ̄τ−=τ−( ̄DX). Then public debt issuances beyond that level

28:1285:78147:21:18:59:563:387:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:of at leasth=ˆD− ̄DˆD∈(   0,1]. Only the safe tranche of public debtˆD(1−h), and only to the extent
28:1286:78246:18:18:59:563:369:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:that it can be isolated through securitization, increases the supply of safe assets and stimulates the
28:1287:78348:18:36:59:105:351:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:economy.
28:1288:78356:36:18:59:563:315:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f30:F:Remark 3Money is a safe assets. At the ZLB, money has the same return as non-monetary safe
28:1289:78446:18:18:59:563:297:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:assets. Money and non-monetary safe assets then become perfect substitutes. One may wonder what
28:1290:78541:18:18:59:563:279:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:happens when the government issues extra money through a “helicopter drop” before the Poisson
28:1291:78634:18:18:59:563:261:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:event  when  the  economy  is  in  a  safety  trap  and  rebates  the  proceeds  lump  sum.   There  are  two
28:1292:78743:18:18:59:563:243:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:options which differ in what the government does once the economy is no longer at the ZLB after
28:1293:78838:18:18:59:563:225:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:the Poisson event: (a) retire the extra money; (b) not retire the extra money. Option (a) is literally
28:1294:78940:18:17:59:563:207:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:identical  to  what  would  happen  if  instead  of  extra  money,  the  government  had  issued  extra  safe
28:1295:79049:17:18:59:563:190:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:short-term debt before the Poisson event and paid it back after the Poisson event. In both cases, the
28:1296:79150:18:18:59:563:172:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:government must raise the same amount of extra taxes after the Poisson event to either retire the
28:1297:79247:18:18:59:563:154:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:extra money or pay back the extra debt.  This stimulates the economy before the Poisson event in
28:1298:79343:18:18:59:563:136:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:a safety trap.  To analyze option (b) we must use the modification of the model introduced later in
28:1299:79442:18:19:59:563:118:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:Section4 which allows for capacity over-utilization as well as capacity under-utilization. Compared
28:1300:79541:19:15:69:563:99:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:F:21If the proceedsˆD−Dof the additional safe debt issuance are rebated to Knightians, then there are no transitional
28:1301:79656:15:12:59:563:84:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:dynamics and the economy jumps immediately to the new stochastic steady state before the Poisson event. Otherwise
28:1302:79769:12:9:59:463:72:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:the new stochastic steady state before the Poisson event is only reached gradually over time.
28:1303:79862:9:15:69:563:63:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:F:22In AppendixA.4, we show that safe public debt issuances can sometimes lead to Pareto improvements, or if not,
28:1304:79973:15:0:59:421:48:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:at least to welfare improvements for certain classes of Utilitarian welfare functions.
29:1305:80061:0:18:59:563:756:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:to option (a), option (b) further stimulates the economy before the Poisson event in a safety trap
29:1306:80159:18:18:59:563:738:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:but at the cost of over-stimulating the economy after the Poisson event.  In other words, there is a
29:1307:80259:18:18:59:563:720:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:policy tradeoff.  This tradeoff is unavoidable:  It it precisely because it over-stimulates the economy
29:1308:80362:18:18:59:563:702:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:after the bad Poisson event that it further increases the value of safe assets and further stimulates
29:1309:80463:18:18:59:563:684:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:the economy before the Poisson event in a safety trap. See AppendixA.2.3for a detailed exposition
29:1310:80560:18:45:59:158:666:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:C:ofthese arguments.
29:1311:80578:45:31:59:236:621:14:g_d0_f9:14:g_d0_f9:C:3.2  Quantitative Easing
29:1312:80602:31:18:59:563:590:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Here we use the term QE loosely to encompass policies that swap risky assets for safe assets such
29:1313:80699:18:18:59:563:572:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:as QE1, LTRO, and many other lender of last resort central bank interventions. We model QE as
29:1314:80792:18:18:59:563:554:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:follows: The government issues additional safe short term debt and purchases private risky assets
29:1315:80889:18:18:59:563:536:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:(the value of which drops to zero after the bad Poisson event). Letˆβgbe the fraction of the value
29:1316:80987:18:31:59:327:518:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f10:B:of risky assets purchased by the government where23
29:1317:81038:31:12:221:347:487:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f17:A:ˆβg[1−[ρ(ˆτ−) + ˆτ−]-−]X
29:1318:81062:12:0:339:344:475:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f17:A:θ
29:1319:81063:0:38:352:402:483:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f17:?:=ˆD−D.
29:1320:81069:38:18:77:563:445:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:The key difference between QE and simply issuing more safe public debt is what the government
29:1321:81162:18:18:59:563:427:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:does with the proceeds from the debt issuance, but the equilibrium rates of returnrandrKand
29:1322:81253:18:18:59:563:409:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:capacity utilizationξare identical. In QE, the government uses the proceeds to purchase private
29:1323:81348:18:18:59:563:391:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:risky assets instead of simply rebating them lump sum to private agents. The revenues from the
29:1324:81442:18:18:59:563:373:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:taxes ˆτbefore the bad Poisson event can be lowered because the government can now avail itself of
29:1325:81540:18:18:59:563:355:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:additional investment revenues from its holdings of private risky assets. Ifτ= 0, as would be the
29:1326:81637:18:18:59:563:337:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:case in a safety trap, then we can get ˆτ <0. This should then be interpreted as a possibility to
29:1327:81734:18:24:59:463:319:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:reduce taxes if there were some other reasons for which taxes had to be raised.
29:1328:81813:24:18:77:563:295:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:As long as there is less than full crowding out, the safe asset shortage is alleviated by this policy:
29:1329:81915:18:18:59:563:277:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f4:B:rKincreases,rdecreases, and the risk premium shrinks. Here QE works not so much by removing
29:1330:82006:18:17:59:563:259:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:risky private assets from private balance sheets, but rather by injecting public assets into private
29:1331:82106:17:18:59:563:242:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:balance sheets. In other words, QE works by increasing the supply of safe assets. The proceeds of
29:1332:82203:18:18:59:572:224:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the extra debt issuance can either be rebated lump sum as in Section3.1  or reinvested in a portfolio
29:1333:82304:18:24:59:309:206:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:of private assets as long as these assets are risky.
29:1334:82356:24:18:77:562:182:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f17:A:If the economy is in a safety trap, QE acts by stimulating output, increasing the value ofξtoˆξ
29:1335:82451:18:18:59:563:164:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:in proportion to the increase in the value of safe assets, exactly as in the case analyzed in Section3.1
29:1336:82555:18:18:59:563:146:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:where the revenues from safe public debt issuance are rebated lump sum instead of being reinvested
29:1337:82653:18:34:59:534:128:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:in a portfolio of private assets as long as these assets are risky and not safe as in this section
29:1338:82751:34:0:277:294:94:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:ˆξ=

29:1342:82765:24:0:69:477:66:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:?:23As long asˆβgis low enough, this can be done without violating the pledgeability condition.
30:1343:82860:0:0:59:259:755:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f18:B:with as beforeˆVS> VSwhereˆVS=-

30:1353:82971:37:18:59:563:701:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f30:F:Remark 4Theseresults in safety traps (constrained regime) are in sharp contrast with liquidity
30:1354:83065:18:18:59:563:683:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f16:F:traps  (unconstrained  regime).   In  our  stylized  setup,  safe  public  debt  issuances  and  QE  haveno
30:1355:83172:18:18:59:563:665:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:effect at all on the recessionξin liquidity traps (the unconstrained regime).  This follows immedi-
30:1356:83271:18:18:59:563:647:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:ately from the fact that the securitization capacityρdoes not show up anywhere in the equilibrium
30:1357:83368:18:18:59:563:629:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:equations in liquidity traps. In our model, the effects of safe public debt issuances and QE in safety
30:1358:83470:18:18:59:563:611:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:traps rely entirely on the (assumed) superior ability of the government to address a form of market
30:1359:83569:18:24:59:431:593:12:g_d0_f30:8:g_d0_f10:C:incompleteness—the difficulty to isolate (macro) safe from risky assets.26
30:1360:83643:24:18:77:563:569:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:A:This irrelevance result relies on our assumption (made throughout the paper) that dividends are
30:1361:83738:18:18:59:563:551:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:taxed while the endowment of newborns (wages) is not.  As a result, safe public debt issuances and
30:1362:83836:18:18:59:563:533:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:QE simply reshuffle the fraction of dividends that accrues to private asset holders and the fraction
30:1363:83936:18:17:59:563:515:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:of dividends that is absorbed by taxes to pay interest on debt of various maturities. This assumption
30:1364:84037:17:18:59:563:498:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:renders our framework de facto Ricardian in the unconstrained regime, despite the fact that we have
30:1365:84136:18:52:59:233:480:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:C:overlapping generations of agents.
30:1366:84170:52:35:59:244:428:17:g_d0_f9:17:g_d0_f9:C:4  Forward Guidance
30:1367:84189:35:18:59:563:393:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Another major policy tool advocated in the context of the ZLB is Forward Guidance (FG): the
30:1368:84280:18:18:59:563:375:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:commitment to low future interest rates once the economy recovers. We show in this section that
30:1369:84375:18:18:59:563:357:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:this policy, which is very effective in liquidity traps, isnotin safety traps. In a nutshell, the reason
30:1370:84479:18:18:59:563:339:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:is that in safety traps the effects of FG are largely dissipated in higher risk premia: The positive
30:1371:84579:18:18:59:563:321:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:effect of higher future asset values on the current value of risky assets is endogenously offset by an
30:1372:84681:18:18:59:563:303:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:increase in risky premia, leaving the current value of risky assets, wealth, and aggregate demand
30:1373:84778:18:24:59:117:285:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:unchanged.
30:1374:84788:24:18:77:563:261:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:We introduce one modification to our model in Section2 (and also drop public debt since it is
30:1375:84881:18:18:59:564:243:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f16:B:not central to our message):Agents now can stretch capacity utilization and produceξt>1units of
30:1376:84976:18:18:59:563:225:12:g_d0_f16:12:g_d0_f16:F:output per unit of non traded input.  This comes at a cost as there is a (proportional separable) per
30:1377:85077:18:18:59:563:207:12:g_d0_f16:12:g_d0_f4:B:period utility loss from capacity utilization overextension, equal tomax{ξt−1,0}.We introduce
30:1378:85170:18:18:59:563:189:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:this modification to capture the standard effects of FG which is to commit to over-stimulating the
30:1379:85268:18:16:69:563:171:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:F:24Because the proceedsˆD−Dof the additional safe debt issuance are not rebated to Knightians, there are
30:1380:85371:16:12:59:563:155:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:transitional dynamics and the new stochastic steady state before the Poisson event is only reached gradually over
30:1381:85484:12:8:59:81:143:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:time.
30:1382:85489:8:16:69:563:135:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:F:25Going back to equation (2), we see that in the limitλ+→0andλ−→0, in a safety trap whenrK= 0, public
30:1383:85590:16:12:59:563:119:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:debt issuances and QE leaver(and hence alsor−rK) unchanged. Whenλ+>0 orλ−>0, additional expected
30:1384:85686:12:8:59:546:107:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:capital gains effects come into play and safe public debt issuances and QE now decreasesr(and hencer−rK).
30:1385:85791:8:16:69:563:99:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:F:26If we allowed the endowments of newborns to be taxed, then safe public debt issuances and QE could have
30:1386:85896:16:12:59:563:83:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:some non-Ricardian effects, depending on exactly how these taxes are levied, and hence affect economic activity in
30:1387:86010:12:12:59:563:71:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:a liquidity trap. For example, Kocherlakota (2013) and Caballero et al. (2015) study non-Ricardian environments
30:1388:86121:12:0:59:393:59:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:where issuing safe public debt can stimulate the economy in a liquidity trap.
31:1389:86200:0:18:59:563:756:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:economy in the future after the good Poisson even when it has exited the ZLB by lowering interest
31:1390:86297:18:24:59:484:738:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:rates, while at the same time preserving all the results that we have derived so far.
31:1391:86382:24:18:77:563:714:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:We assume that the cost is large enough so that under flexible prices, we still haveξt= 1 before
31:1392:86478:18:18:59:562:696:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f10:B:and after the Poisson event, with the same natural allocation as that characterized in Section2.27
31:1393:86576:18:18:59:563:678:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Importantly, with nominal rigidities where output is demanddetermined, this need not be true,
31:1394:86669:18:18:59:563:660:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:depending on the stance of monetary policy. The equilibrium conditions are then identical to those
31:1395:86767:18:18:59:563:642:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:in Section2, but with the possibility that capacity utilization exceedsone before or after the Poisson

32:1466:90228:24:18:77:563:523:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:A safety trap is addressed more directly by committing to provide support during bad rather
32:1467:90319:18:18:59:563:505:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:than good times, as would be the case of a commitment to lower interesti−trates after the bad

32:1469:90505:18:18:59:563:469:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:ability to lower interest rates in that state. If indeed the bad state happens to coincide with yet
32:1470:90604:18:18:59:563:451:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:another safety or liquidity trap, monetary authorities could find themselves unable to deliver a lower
32:1471:90706:18:37:59:240:433:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:interest rate (see AppendixA.3  ).
32:1472:90740:37:18:59:563:396:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f30:F:Remark 5These results in safety traps (constrained regime) are,  again,  in sharp contrast with
