32:1488:91017:38:18:77:563:277:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:A:Committingto low interest rates after the good Poisson event increases future value of assets
32:1489:91110:18:18:59:563:259:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:after the good Poisson event.  In contrast to the safety trap case, this also increases the value of
32:1490:91210:18:18:59:563:241:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:assets before the Poisson event while the economy is in the liquidity trap. This wealth effect increases
32:1491:91314:18:18:59:563:223:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:demand and mitigates the recession.  Forward guidance works by alleviating the asset shortage that
32:1492:91412:18:18:59:563:205:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:is at the root of the recession.  It trades off a future boom (output above potential) after the good
32:1493:91513:18:15:59:500:187:12:g_d0_f30:8:g_d0_f10:C:Poisson event against a mitigation of the recession (output below potential) before it.31
32:1494:91602:15:16:69:563:172:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:F:29There is one caveat to this conclusion. We have assumed that prices are entirely rigid. If prices could adjust
32:1495:91714:16:12:59:563:156:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:gradually over time in a forward looking manner, then forward guidance could regain some kick: A commitment to
32:1496:91824:12:12:59:563:144:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:lower interest rates after the good Poisson event could increase inflation while the economy is in a safety trap. This
32:1497:91942:12:12:59:563:132:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:would lower the safe interest raterKand mitigate the recession. Note than when we model inflation in Section5, we
32:1498:92055:12:12:59:563:120:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:assume, motivated by a desire to capture downward wage rigidity, that inflation is determined by a myopic Philipps
32:1499:92169:12:12:59:472:108:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:curve rather than an expectations-augmented Philipps curve, so that this effect does not arise.
32:1500:92264:12:12:69:563:96:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:A similar comment applies to the unconventional tax policies considered by Correia et al.  (2012), which here
32:1501:92373:12:12:59:563:84:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:could simply take the form of an increasing path of sales taxes—say through a sales tax holiday—which would create
32:1502:92487:12:8:59:277:72:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:inflation in consumer prices and hence reducerK.
32:1503:92535:8:12:69:370:64:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:?:30In AppendixA.4, we show that FG is Pareto dominated by no FG.

33:1505:92704:0:36:59:160:756:17:g_d0_f9:17:g_d0_f9:C:5  Inflation
33:1506:92716:36:18:59:563:720:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:In this section we relax the extreme sticky price rigidity assumption and show how safety traps trig-
33:1507:92817:18:18:59:563:702:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:ger deflationary forces, which exacerbate the output drop. We also show that the policy multiplier

33:1510:93115:45:31:59:410:621:14:g_d0_f9:14:g_d0_f9:C:5.1  Safety Trap, Deflation, and Inflation Targets
33:1511:93165:31:18:59:563:590:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:We assume that prices cannot fall faster than at a certain pace:πt≥ −(κ0+κ1(1−ξt)), with
33:1512:93253:18:18:59:563:572:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f4:B:κ1>0   . The more slack there is in the economy, the more prices can fall. We impose that if there
33:1513:93351:18:18:59:563:554:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:is slack in the economy, prices fall as fast as they can: I.e.,ξt<1    impliesπt=−(κ0+κ1(1−ξt)).
33:1514:93447:18:33:59:435:536:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:We capture this requirement with the complementary slackness condition
33:1515:93517:33:33:222:400:503:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f17:A:[πt+ (κ0+κ1(1−ξt))](1−ξt) = 0.
33:1516:93547:33:18:59:563:470:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:This is a traditional upward sloping Phillips curve relating inflationπtand capacity utilizationξt.
33:1517:93646:18:17:59:563:452:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:The Phillips curve becomes vertical atξt= 1. Our motivation is to capture downward nominal
33:1518:93736:17:18:59:563:435:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:rigidities. This specification of the Phillips curve can be justified by appealing to a “nominal social
33:1519:93839:18:18:59:563:417:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:norm”, which can only be slowly revised downward over time, so that agents would never accept
33:1520:93932:18:18:59:563:399:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:setting prices falling faster than−(κ0+κ1(1−ξt)) per unit of time. Ifκ1= 0 andκ0= 0, this
33:1521:94021:18:18:59:563:381:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:corresponds to complete downward nominal rigidities. Ifκ0= 0 andκ1=∞,this corresponds
33:1522:94106:18:18:59:563:363:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:to the case of perfectly flexible prices. This modeling strategy and the results that follow borrows
33:1523:94206:18:24:59:292:345:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:heavily from Eggertsson and Mehrota (2014).

35:1581:96795:18:18:59:563:684:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:either one or three intersections between the supply and demand curves. We have already seen the
35:1582:96891:18:18:59:563:666:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:bad equilibrium. The other equilibria, which exist if the inflation target is high enoughπ∗≥−rK,n,
35:1583:96989:18:24:59:207:648:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f10:B:featureπ >−κ0andξ=1.32
35:1584:97011:24:18:77:563:624:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:To summarize, when−κ0+rK,n<0   , there is always a safety trap equilibrium withξ <1 and
35:1585:97098:18:18:59:563:606:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f4:B:π <−κ0≤π∗and it is locally determinate. If the inflation target is high enough (0≤rK,n+π∗),
35:1586:97189:18:17:59:563:588:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:then there are also two other equilibria withξ= 1 with two different nominal interest rates (i= 0
35:1587:97286:17:18:59:563:571:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:andi=rK,n+π∗>0   ) and two different inflation rates (π=−rK,nandπ=π∗), but only the
35:1588:97369:18:18:59:563:553:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:latter is locally determinate. In other words, the increase in the inflation target needs to be large
35:1589:97470:18:18:59:563:535:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:enough to even have a chance to work. Note however that even when there is a “good” equilibrium
35:1590:97565:18:18:59:563:517:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:withξ= 1 andi=rK,n+π∗>0   , the “bad” equilibrium withξ <1 andi= 0 still exists because
35:1591:97652:18:18:59:563:499:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:expectations of low inflation are self-fulfilling: Starting from the “good” equilibrium, low enough
35:1592:97751:18:18:59:563:481:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:expected inflation increases the real interest rate despite the reduction of the nominal interest
35:1593:97848:18:18:59:563:463:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:rate to zero, depresses the economy, which in turn generates low inflation. Policy cannot select
35:1594:97944:18:18:59:563:445:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:among these equilibria: The best a high inflation target can achieve is the possibility of a good
35:1595:98041:18:18:59:563:427:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:equilibrium, not the elimination of the possibility of the bad equilibrium.33,34Figure4 provides a
35:1596:98139:18:18:59:563:409:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:graphical illustration. In the figure, equilibrium inflation in the safety trap equilibrium is negative
35:1597:98242:18:24:59:212:391:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:but this need not be the case.
35:1598:98272:24:18:77:563:367:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:We can connect this discussion with the Keynesian cross equilibrium representation developed
35:1599:98364:18:18:59:563:349:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:in Section2, which can still be used withrK=i−πonce inflationπhas been solved out. Given
35:1600:98452:18:17:59:563:331:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:nominal interest ratesi, higher inflation helps to reduce safe interest rates, causing an upward shift
35:1601:98554:17:18:59:563:314:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:in aggregate demand and resulting in a increase in output. WhenrK,n<0andπ∗>−rK,nin
35:1602:98636:18:18:59:563:296:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the good equilibrium, this logic is strong enough to generate a low enough safe real interest rate
35:1603:98734:18:18:59:563:278:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f4:B:rK=rK,n. But in the bad safety trap equilibrium withi=0 andπ <−κ0≤π∗, it is not. In fact,
35:1604:98823:18:18:59:563:260:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:when−κ0<0   , this logic can work in reverse, with the recession causing deflation, increasing safe
35:1605:98922:18:24:59:522:242:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:real interest ratesrK=−π>0 , reducing aggregate demand, further reducing output etc.
35:1606:99006:24:18:77:563:218:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:Also note that adding an inflation channel to the modelincreasesthe value of the Keynesian
35:1607:99096:18:12:59:123:200:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:multiplier to

35:1612:99124:22:7:69:391:150:7:g_d0_f12:7:g_d0_f12:?:32In an equilibrium withπ >0 andξ= 1,inflation is determined byπ=1
35:1613:99190:7:0:381:412:143:7:g_d0_f38:10:g_d0_f37:?:φ−1[φπ

35:1615:99223:17:12:59:563:133:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:(in which casei=rK,n+π∗+φ(π−π∗)) or byπ=−rK,nifrK,n+π∗+φ(π−π∗)≤0 (in which casei= 0). The

35:1617:99393:9:15:69:563:112:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:F:33This multiplicity is also present, and for similar reasons, in the analysis of liquidity traps in Eggertsson and
35:1618:99507:15:9:59:130:97:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:Mehrota (2014).
35:1619:99522:9:15:69:563:88:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:F:34In AppendixA.4, we show that increases in the inflation target can sometimes lead to Pareto improvements,
35:1620:99629:15:12:59:563:73:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:or if not, at least to welfare improvements for certain classes of Utilitarian welfare functions. We also show that
35:1621:99744:12:12:59:563:61:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:they always lead to Pareto improvements if lump sum taxes are available to redistribute among Neutrals and among
35:1622:99856:12:0:59:197:49:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:Knightians in any given period.
36:1623:99889:0:11:59:175:756:12:g_d0_f4:6:g_d0_f32:B:so thatd(ξX) =11−κ1ξ
36:1624:99909:11:0:160:179:745:6:g_d0_f32:6:g_d0_f32:?:θ−rK
36:1625:99913:0:9:186:197:761:8:g_d0_f18:8:g_d0_f18:?:ξX
36:1626:99915:9:0:184:220:752:8:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f17:?:θVSθdV
36:1627:99921:0:25:222:563:760:8:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f4:A:S. This is because an increase in the value of safe assets, increases
36:1628:99990:25:18:59:563:735:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:aggregate demand, which increases output, increasing inflation, reducing the safe real interest rate,
36:1629:100091:18:18:59:563:717:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:further increasing aggregate demand and output etc. ad infinitum. The more responsive is inflation
36:1630:100189:18:18:59:563:699:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:to capacity utilizationξ(the larger isκ1), the larger is the Keynesian multiplier. In other words,
36:1631:100287:18:45:59:450:681:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:increased price flexibility is destabilizing as in DeLong and Summers (1986).
36:1632:100364:45:31:59:482:636:14:g_d0_f9:14:g_d0_f9:C:5.2  Public Debt, QE and Forward Guidance with Inflation
36:1633:100420:31:18:59:563:605:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:We now turn to the effects of the policies considered in Sections3 and4 in this extended model
36:1634:100514:18:18:59:563:587:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:with inflation. We focus on the safety trap equilibrium and show that the main conclusions remain
36:1635:100611:18:24:59:357:569:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:qualitatively unchanged but the power of QE is enhanced.
36:1636:100667:24:18:77:563:545:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:We start with safe public debt and QE. In a safety trap,ξ <1 andπ <0 are determined by the
36:1637:100757:18:43:59:295:527:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:intersection of the demand and supply curves:

36:1639:100811:0:0:299:318:495:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f5:?:α−

36:1645:100835:43:26:252:369:441:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f17:A:π=−(κ0+κ1(1−ξ)).
36:1646:100851:26:18:59:563:415:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Clearly, increasingDtoˆD  > D(and either rebating the proceeds to consumers or purchasing
36:1647:100940:18:18:59:563:397:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:private risky assets) shifts the demand curve down which, given that it is steeper than the supply
36:1648:101038:18:18:59:563:379:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:curve, results in an increase inξtoˆξ > ξ. Note that the stimulus is stronger in this extended setup

36:1660:101202:7:0:235:254:305:8:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f17:?:θv

36:1662:101208:8:14:266:563:305:8:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f4:A:X). This is because of a virtuous cycle whereby additional
36:1663:101266:14:18:59:563:291:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:safe assets increase output, which increases inflation (reduces deflation), which lowers the real
36:1664:101363:18:18:59:563:273:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:interest, further stimulating output etc. ad infinitum, resulting in a larger value of the Keynesian
36:1665:101463:18:24:59:212:255:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:multiplier as explained above.
36:1666:101493:24:18:77:563:231:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:We turn next to forward guidance. In order for monetary policy to be able to generate a boom
36:1667:101585:18:17:59:563:213:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:after the good Poisson event, we introduce the following modification of our setup. We assume that
36:1668:101683:17:33:59:457:196:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the Phillips curve only becomes vertical at a value ̄ξ >1 so that we now have
36:1669:101760:33:33:222:400:163:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f17:A:[πt+ (κ0+κ1(1−ξt))]( ̄ξ−ξt) = 0.
36:1670:101792:33:24:59:529:130:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Furthermore, we assume thatκ0=−π∗so that inflation isπ∗if the economy is at capacity.
36:1671:101877:24:18:77:563:106:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:To capture forward guidance, we continue to assume that monetary policy follows the truncated
36:1672:101970:18:18:59:115:88:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Taylor rule
36:1673:101981:18:0:220:402:70:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f5:A:it= max{0,rK,nt+π∗+φ(πt−π∗)}
37:1674:102011:0:18:59:563:756:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:before and after the bad Poisson event, but we allow monetary policy to depart from this rule after
37:1675:102110:18:33:59:541:738:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the good Poisson event and follow instead (recall thatrK,nt=δθafter the good Poisson event)
37:1676:102201:33:33:223:399:705:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f5:A:i+t= max{0,ˆı+t+π∗+φ(πt−π∗)}
37:1677:102229:33:18:59:563:672:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:where ˆı+t< δθforσ+≤t≤σ++Tand ˆı+t=δθfort > σ++T.Then output is above potential
37:1678:102308:18:26:59:484:654:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:after the good Poisson event. Capacity utilization satisfies the differential equation
37:1679:102394:26:19:214:219:628:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f18:A: ̇ξ+t

37:1681:102402:0:0:228:237:617:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:?:=
37:1682:102403:0:10:241:246:627:12:g_d0_f34:12:g_d0_f34:?:(

37:1685:102412:10:37:291:412:617:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f17:A:+ (φ−1) (πt−π∗)≤0,
37:1686:102430:37:26:248:374:580:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f4:A:πt−π∗+κ1(1−ξ+t) = 0
37:1687:102449:26:24:59:239:554:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:with terminal conditionξ+σ++T= 1.
37:1688:102482:24:17:77:563:530:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:Just as in Section4, the solution featuresξ+t>1andπt≥π∗forσ+≤t< σ++T.The
37:1689:102554:17:18:59:563:513:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:rest of the analysis is identical and the conclusion is identical. Forward guidance stimulates the
37:1690:102652:18:18:59:563:495:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:economy after the good Poisson event, resulting in a boom and inflation above target. But this fails
37:1691:102752:18:32:59:482:477:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:to stimulate the economy before the Poisson when the economy is in a safety trap.
37:1692:102833:32:18:59:563:445:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f30:F:Remark 6We could also introduce inflation in the unconstrained regime and liquidity traps. Just
37:1693:102928:18:18:59:563:427:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:like in the constrained regime,  when the natural safe interest rate is negativerK,n<0,there is
37:1694:103023:18:18:59:563:409:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:always a bad liquidity trap equilibrium with a recessionξ <1and deflationπ <0.  If the inflation
37:1695:103119:18:18:59:563:391:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:target ̄πis high enough, there is also a good equilibrium with no recessionξ= 1and inflation at
37:1696:103214:18:18:59:564:373:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:targetπ=  ̄π.  Introducing inflation does not change the results that safe public debt and QE are
37:1697:103311:18:18:59:563:355:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:F:ineffective in liquidity traps. Forward guidance gains an extra kick by increasing inflation, reducing
37:1698:103413:18:50:59:419:337:12:g_d0_f30:12:g_d0_f30:C:real interest rates, further stimulating output and inflation, and so on.
37:1699:103486:50:36:59:319:287:17:g_d0_f9:17:g_d0_f9:C:6  Extensions and Robustness
37:1700:103514:36:18:59:563:251:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:In the appendix we present two extensions, which we briefly summarize here: an analysis of the
37:1701:103608:18:18:59:563:233:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:role of bubbles (AppendixA.5  ) and an endogenization of the securitization process to demonstrate
37:1702:103706:18:18:59:575:215:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the presence of a securitization externality (AppendixA.6  ). We also comment on the robustness of
37:1703:103804:18:24:59:116:197:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:our results.
37:1704:103816:24:18:77:563:173:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:A:Bubbles and fiscal capacity.The very low interest rates that characterize a safety trap
37:1705:103903:18:18:59:563:155:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:raises the issue of whether speculative bubbles may emerge, and whether these can play a useful
37:1706:103998:18:18:59:576:137:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:role through their wealth effect. We show in AppendixA.5   that bubbles can indeed arise in safety
37:1707:104096:18:17:59:563:119:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:traps, but that only the emergence of safe bubbles (as opposed to risky bubbles) can stimulate
37:1708:104190:17:18:59:563:102:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:economic activity. This is because only safe bubbles alleviate the shortage of safe assets while risky
37:1709:104292:18:18:59:563:84:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:bubbles end up simply crowding out other risky assets. The fact that risky bubbles have no effect on
37:1710:104392:18:18:59:563:66:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:output in a safety trap formalizes some observations in Summers (2013) that in secular stagnation
37:1711:104489:18:0:59:563:48:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:environments, even large financial bubbles only seem to create moderate economic expansions. It
38:1712:104586:0:18:59:563:756:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:stands in contrast to standard liquidity trap environments, where both safe and risky bubbles
38:1713:104679:18:18:59:563:738:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:stimulate output. This is because in standard liquidity trap environments, both increase total asset
38:1714:104779:18:24:59:337:720:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:supply and alleviate the underlying shortage of assets.
38:1715:104834:24:18:77:563:696:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:We associate safe bubbles to (some) safe public debt: The existence of a bubbly-region where
38:1716:104926:18:18:59:563:678:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the safe real interest rate is permanently below the growth rate of the economy is equivalent to an
38:1717:105025:18:18:59:563:660:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:expansion of the fiscal capacity of the government who can issue some amount of safe debt without
38:1718:105122:18:24:59:193:642:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:ever having to raise taxes.
38:1719:105149:24:18:77:575:618:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:A:Securitization externality.In AppendixA.6   we endogenize the securitization capacity of the
38:1720:105241:18:18:59:563:600:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:economy. We assume that by investing resourcesjtXdt,a Neutral agent can increaseρ(jt) and,
38:1721:105331:18:17:59:562:582:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:with it, increase the supply of safe assets (i.e., the share of the tree’s revenue in the bad state of
38:1722:105433:17:24:59:237:565:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the world that is pledgable today).
38:1723:105468:24:18:77:563:541:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:We show in this extension that outside of a safety trap, the competitive equilibrium is constrained
38:1724:105567:18:18:59:563:523:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Pareto efficient, but that in a safety trap, it is constrained inefficient (there is underprovision of safe
38:1725:105674:18:18:59:563:505:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:assets). We trace back this inefficiency to asecuritization externality. In a safety trap, private agents
38:1726:105779:18:18:59:563:487:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:do not internalize the full social benefit of creating safe assets. More specifically, they do not take
38:1727:105882:18:18:59:563:469:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:into account the stimulative effects of these assets. This market failure builds a case for government
38:1728:105984:18:18:59:563:451:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:intervention in securitization markets. The government could use taxes or quantity restrictions to
38:1729:106082:18:18:59:563:433:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:encourage securitization, force financial institutions to raise more fresh capital than they would
38:1730:106180:18:18:59:563:415:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:do otherwise or directly recapitalize them to boost their securitization capacity, or simply directly
38:1731:106281:18:18:59:563:397:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:engage in securitization through QE. This argument is distinct from the comparative advantage of
38:1732:106377:18:24:59:407:379:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the government in safe asset creation that we analyzed in Section3.
38:1733:106444:24:18:77:563:355:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:A:Robustness.Our model is stylized, which allows us to isolate and illustrate the key mecha-
38:1734:106534:18:17:59:563:337:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:nisms, and to bring out most clearly the differences between safety traps and liquidity traps. Of
38:1735:106631:17:18:59:563:320:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:course, its stark assumptions are likely to hold in a milder form in practice, and it is important to
38:1736:106732:18:24:59:377:302:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:understand how our results would be altered in such contexts.
38:1737:106793:24:18:77:563:278:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:The fundamental features of our model, which drive our results, are the following: (i) nominal
38:1738:106887:18:18:59:563:260:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:rigidities and a ZLB; (ii) macroeconomic uncertainty and risk aversion; (iii) heterogeneity in risk
38:1739:106986:18:18:59:563:242:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:aversion with risk tolerant and risk averse agents; (iv) financial frictions hampering securitization.
38:1740:107088:18:18:59:563:224:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Features (i) and (ii) are standard, although they are rarely combined in standard liquidity trap
38:1741:107184:18:18:59:563:206:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:analyses which rely on perfect foresight or log-linearizations. Feature (iii) gives rise to risk sharing
38:1742:107288:18:18:59:563:188:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:through asset markets, and in particular through the issuance of zero-net-supply safe assets from
38:1743:107385:18:18:59:563:170:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:risk tolerant agents to risk averse agents (one could imagine either the issuance of entirely safe
38:1744:107483:18:18:59:563:152:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:assets as in our model and also as in Barro and Mollerus 2014, or simply of safer assets than the
38:1745:107580:18:18:59:563:134:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:positive-net-supply Lucas trees). Feature (iv) hampers this securitization process by limiting the
38:1746:107678:18:24:59:327:116:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:collateral that can be used to back these safe assets.
38:1747:107732:24:17:77:563:92:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:We model macroeconomic uncertainty in feature (ii) as a macroeconomic Poisson event, and we
38:1748:107823:17:18:59:563:75:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:assume that all uncertainty is resolved at once after this Poisson event. The safety trap then only
38:1749:107922:18:0:59:563:57:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:arises before the Poisson event, precisely because a bad Poisson event might occur in the future.
39:1750:108021:0:18:59:563:756:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:At the cost of analytical tractability, one could allow for more general stochastic processes, and
39:1751:108119:18:18:59:563:738:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:relax the assumption that uncertainty is resolved all at once with the realization of the event. For
39:1752:108219:18:18:59:563:720:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:example, if another Poisson event could occur after the first Poisson event, then the economy could
39:1753:108318:18:18:59:563:702:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:end up in a safety trap not only before the first realization of the Poisson event, but also after the
39:1754:108420:18:18:59:563:684:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:realization of the first bad Poisson event, because another future bad Poisson event might occur.
39:1755:108517:18:18:59:563:666:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:The resulting compounding of macroeconomic uncertainty would further reduce safe asset supply,
39:1756:108611:18:18:59:563:648:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:and trigger an even bigger recession before the first Poisson event. Output after the first bad Poisson
39:1757:108714:18:18:59:563:630:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:event would also be lower, not only because of the exogenous impact of the first bad Poisson event,
39:1758:108813:18:24:59:288:612:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:but also because of an endogenous recession.
39:1759:108857:24:17:77:563:588:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:In our model, features (iii) and (iv) take an extreme form: agents are either risk neutral or
39:1760:108950:17:18:59:563:571:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:infinitely risk averse; and there is a hard securitization constraint. In addition, we have assumed
39:1761:109049:18:18:59:563:553:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:that agents do not substitute consumption intertemporally. These extreme assumptions make the
39:1762:109142:18:18:59:563:535:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:model tractable and transparent, and allow us to derive our results in closed form. Milder versions
39:1763:109241:18:18:59:563:517:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:of these features would lead to milder forms of our main results: recessions at the ZLB associated
39:1764:109339:18:18:59:563:499:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:with increases in risk premia generated by shortages of safe assets; stimulative effects of safe debt
39:1765:109440:18:18:59:563:481:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:issuances and QE; reduced effectiveness of FG. For example, and focusing on FG, with finite dif-
39:1766:109536:18:18:59:563:463:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:ferences in risk aversion, FG would increase the attractiveness of risky assets and hence reduce the
39:1767:109636:18:18:59:563:445:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:demand of safe assets by risk averse agents, thereby stimulating the economy, the more so, the
39:1768:109730:18:18:59:563:427:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:lower the risk aversion of risk averse agents, and the higher the intertemporal elasticity of substi-
39:1769:109831:18:18:59:575:409:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:tution. Likewise, with an active investment margin to relax financial frictions as in AppendixA.6  ,
39:1770:109931:18:18:59:563:391:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:FG would increase the incentives of risk tolerant agents to invest in securitization and issue safe
39:1771:110030:18:18:59:563:373:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:assets to capture risk premia, increase the supply of safe assets, and hence stimulate the economy,
39:1772:110129:18:18:59:563:355:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the more so, the higher the elasticity of securitization capacity to investment or, equivalently, the
39:1773:110230:18:17:59:563:337:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:responsiveness of the supply of safe assets to risk premia. Similar observations apply to safe debt
39:1774:110329:17:18:59:563:320:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:issuances and QE. In particular, it is no longer key that public debt be absolutely safe in order to
39:1775:110429:18:18:59:563:302:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:stimulate output: It is enough that it be safer (lower beta) than the private risky assets that are
39:1776:110528:18:51:59:345:284:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:being purchased with the proceeds of the debt issuance.
39:1777:110583:51:36:59:212:233:17:g_d0_f9:17:g_d0_f9:C:7  Final Remarks
39:1778:110599:36:18:59:563:197:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:In this paper we provide a model that captures some of the most salient macroeconomic consequences
39:1779:110697:18:18:59:563:179:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:and policy implications of a safety trap. The model is deliberately highly stylized, which allows us
39:1780:110797:18:18:59:563:161:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:to isolate the specific role of safe asset shortages at the ZLB. Safety traps correspond to liquidity
39:1781:110898:18:18:59:563:143:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:traps in which the emergence of an endogenous risk premium significantly alters the connection
39:1782:110992:18:23:59:378:125:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:between macroeconomic policy, wealth, and economic activity.
39:1783:111052:23:18:77:563:102:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:In a nutshell, in a situation of safety trap, private agents (and some sovereigns) want to substitute
39:1784:111153:18:18:59:563:84:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:some of their risky holdings for safer ones. In the absence of mechanisms to lower safe interest rates
39:1785:111255:18:18:59:563:66:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:to restore equilibrium, the most powerful policies are those that help the private sector implement
39:1786:111354:18:0:59:563:48:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:this swap. As we mentioned in the main text, the early QE policies implemented by the FED during
40:1787:111452:0:18:59:563:756:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the subprime crises did just that, and there is extensive evidence of their effectiveness. Another
40:1788:111550:18:18:59:563:738:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:successful example is the OMT (outright monetary transactions) program established by the ECB
40:1789:111643:18:18:59:563:720:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:in late 2012, which had an immediate impact on the Eurozone risk perception, or the more recent
40:1790:111738:18:24:59:367:702:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:(April 2016) move of the ECB to purchase corporate bonds.
40:1791:111795:24:18:77:563:678:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:However, over time and partly as a result of lack of political support, asset purchase policies
40:1792:111890:18:18:59:563:660:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:have turned mostly into swaps of one form of safe asset for another, which is not nearly as effective
40:1793:111991:18:18:59:563:642:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:in a safety trap context. In fact, in a previous version of this paper (Caballero and Farhi 2013), we
40:1794:112092:18:18:59:563:624:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:argued that Operation Twist (OT) type polices, where the FED purchases long maturity Treasuries
40:1795:112187:18:18:59:563:606:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:and sells short maturity ones, could be counterproductive. The reason is that long-term public debt,
40:1796:112287:18:17:59:563:588:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:while risky, is anegative-betaasset. OT type policies boil down to swapping negative-beta assets
40:1797:112383:17:18:59:563:571:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:for zero-beta assets, which reduces the effective supply of safe assets. By contrast, the right form of
40:1798:112486:18:18:59:563:553:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:QE policies entails swapping positive-beta assets for zero-beta assets, which increases the effective
40:1799:112587:18:24:59:166:535:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:supply of safe assets.
40:1800:112609:24:18:77:563:511:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:Similarly, forward guidance policies are largely ineffective and can be seen as a mostly failed
40:1801:112704:18:18:59:563:493:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:attempts at stimulating the economy by attempting to increase the value of risky assets, which are
40:1802:112802:18:24:59:358:475:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:essentially dissipated in offsetting increases in risk premia.
40:1803:112864:24:18:77:563:451:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:Sufficient increases in the inflation target, by reducing safe real interest rates, are effective at
40:1804:112964:18:18:59:563:433:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:stimulating output. The same goes for imposing negative interest ratesrK<0   , to the extent that
40:1805:113061:18:18:59:563:415:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:it is possible. Recently, some countries have experimented with modest levels of negative interest
40:1806:113159:18:18:59:563:397:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:rates. At this stage, it is unclear exactly how far below zero interest rates can go. Of course safety
40:1807:113261:18:18:59:563:379:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:traps can emerge even if the lower bound is not exactly at zero, as long as there is some finite lower
40:1808:113363:18:24:59:94:361:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:bound.
40:1809:113369:24:17:77:579:337:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:Given the faster growth of safe-asset-consumer economies than that of safe-asset-producer economies
40:1810:113468:17:18:59:563:320:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:as well as the aging of wealth-rich economies, absent major financial innovations, the shortage of
40:1811:113566:18:18:59:563:302:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:safe assets is only likely to worsen over time, perhaps as a latent factor during booms but reemerging
40:1812:113668:18:18:59:563:284:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:in full force during contractions. It is our conjecture that the shortage of safe assets will remain as
40:1813:113771:18:18:59:563:266:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:a structural drag, lowering safe rates, increasing safety spreads, straining the financial system, and
40:1814:113873:18:0:59:472:248:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:weakening the effectiveness of conventional monetary policy during contractions.

56:2618:140543:18:18:59:563:446:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:potential, the extra money increases wealth, which increases consumption, which stimulates output,
56:2619:140641:18:18:59:563:428:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:increases the value of the dividend of the Lucas’ trees, increases the value of Lucas’ trees, which
56:2620:140740:18:18:59:563:410:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:further increases wealth, etc. This feedback loop settles at a new fixed point with higher output
56:2621:140837:18:24:59:356:392:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:above potential and higher capacity utilization above one.
56:2622:140895:24:18:77:563:368:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:Given that it stimulates output after the Poisson event, option (b) increases the cash flows hat

57:2674:141956:0:18:59:563:756:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:economy exits the safety trap further mitigates the recession associated with the safety trap. How-
57:2675:142055:18:18:59:563:738:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:ever, this extra effectiveness is not a free lunch, as it comes with the important cost of excessively
57:2676:142157:18:45:59:337:720:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:stimulating the economy when it exits the safety trap.
57:2677:142211:45:32:59:375:675:14:g_d0_f9:14:g_d0_f9:C:A.3  Supporting Asset Values in Bad Times

57:2680:142444:18:17:59:563:607:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:after the bad Poisson event.35By setting the nominal interest ratei−tbelow the natural interest

57:2697:142980:18:24:59:134:429:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f10:B:by-−ξ−σ+).36,37
57:2698:142995:24:18:77:563:405:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:However, it is natural to question whether monetary authorities would have the ability to lower
57:2699:143090:18:18:59:563:387:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:interest rates in that state. If indeed the bad state happens to coincide with yet another safety or
57:2700:143190:18:18:59:562:369:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f10:B:liquidity trap, monetary authorities could find themselves unable to deliver a lower interest rate.38
57:2701:143291:18:15:69:563:351:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:F:35Another example is the OMT (outright monetary transactions) program established by the ECB in late 2012,
57:2702:143397:15:9:59:345:336:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:which had an immediate impact on the Eurozone risk perception.
57:2703:143459:9:15:69:563:327:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:F:36There are transitional dynamics before the Poisson event when forward guidance is announced, which we do
57:2704:143565:15:12:59:563:312:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:not report in the interest of space.  After the (future) policy announcement, the economy first goes through a
57:2705:143675:12:12:59:563:300:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:phase where it is in the unconstrained regime for a while because because Knightian wealth only increases gradually
57:2706:143790:12:12:59:563:288:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:over time while the value of safe assets jumps up immediately. But conditional on no Poisson event occuring, the
57:2707:143902:12:12:59:563:276:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:economy eventually re-enters the constrained regime as Knightian wealth increases. All variables converge to their
57:2708:144016:12:9:59:298:264:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:new stochastic steady state values gradually over time.
57:2709:144071:9:15:69:563:255:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:F:37Note we could just as well have used the model with public debt. The central banker’s put works by increasing
57:2710:144182:15:8:59:344:240:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:both the public and private sectors’ ability to provide safe assets.
57:2711:144250:8:16:69:563:232:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:F:38Perhaps a more realistic policy option would be a commitment by the authorities to buy up safe assets at an
57:2712:144359:16:13:59:563:216:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:inflated price after the Poisson events—a form of government (central bank?) put. A commitment to buy up safe
57:2713:144468:13:12:59:562:203:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f37:F:private assets at an inflated valueω−ρμ−Xθ> ρμ−Xθwould mitigate the recession and increase the value ofξtoˆξ
57:2714:144576:12:9:59:84:191:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:where
57:2715:144581:9:21:284:340:182:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f37:A:ˆξ=ω−ξ > ξ.
57:2716:144592:21:12:59:563:161:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:It could be carried out by monetary authorities but it does require spare fiscal capacity (in the form of taxes or
57:2717:144706:12:12:59:563:149:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:seigniorage).  This kind of public insurance policy can potentially play a crucial role in a safety trap.  See, e.g.,
57:2718:144823:12:12:59:563:137:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:Caballero and Kurlat (2010) for a proposal to increase the resilience of the financial system in a shortage of safe
57:2719:144938:12:12:59:563:125:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:assets environment. Also, see Brunnermeir et al (2012) for a related proposal in the context of the current Euro
57:2720:145050:12:0:59:83:113:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:crisis.
58:2721:145059:0:32:59:154:756:14:g_d0_f9:14:g_d0_f9:C:A.4  Welfare
58:2722:145071:32:18:59:563:724:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:In this section, we analyze the welfare properties of the different policies that we have considered.
58:2723:145172:18:18:59:563:706:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:We treat the case of public debt issuances, increases in the inflation target, and FG. The analysis
58:2724:145271:18:18:59:563:688:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:for QE is more complex because it features nontrivial transitional dynamics. We focus on safety
58:2725:145366:18:18:59:563:670:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:traps when the economy is in the constrained regime against the ZLB atrK= 0. We also focus on
58:2726:145459:18:23:59:213:652:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the limitλ+→0andλ−→0    .
58:2727:145484:23:18:77:563:629:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:A:Public debt issuance.After a public debt issuanceˆD > D, there is no transitional dynamics,
58:2728:145575:18:18:59:563:611:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:so that the economy jumps immediately to a new stochastic steady state before the Poisson event,
58:2729:145671:18:18:59:563:593:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:and also to a steady state after the Poisson event. Before the Poisson event it, increases output
58:2730:145768:18:11:59:563:575:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:toˆξX=ˆDDξX > ξX,increases Neutral and Knightian wealth toˆWN=ˆDDWN> WNandˆWK=
58:2731:145846:11:11:62:67:564:8:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f18:F:ˆD
58:2732:145848:11:0:60:80:553:8:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f17:C:DW
58:2733:145850:0:22:81:563:561:8:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f4:A:K> WK, leavesrandrKunchanged. After the Poisson event it leaves output and interest
58:2734:145933:22:18:59:563:539:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:rates unchanged. These imply that: Neutrals and Knightians that are already born at the time of
58:2735:146028:18:18:59:563:521:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the public debt issuance are strictly better off (their wealth jumps up at impact and the rates of
58:2736:146126:18:18:59:563:503:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:return on their wealth is unchanged going forward); Neutrals and Knightians that are born after
58:2737:146221:18:18:59:563:485:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:the public debt issuance but before the Poisson event are strictly better off (their income when
58:2738:146317:18:18:59:563:467:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:newborn is higher and the rates of return on their wealth is unchanged); Neutrals and Knightians
58:2739:146413:18:18:59:563:449:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:that are born after the public debt issuance and the Poisson event are as well off (their income
58:2740:146509:18:24:59:481:431:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f10:B:when newborn is identical and the rates of return on their wealth is unchanged).39
58:2741:146591:24:17:77:563:407:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:A:Increase in the inflation target.After an increase in the inflation target that creates the
58:2742:146682:17:18:59:563:390:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:possibility of a good equilibrium, assuming that the economy moves to that equilibrium, there is
58:2743:146778:18:18:59:563:372:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:no transitional dynamics, so that the economy jumps immediately to a new stochastic steady state
58:2744:146874:18:18:59:563:354:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:before the Poisson event, and also to a steady state after the Poisson event. Before the Poisson event
58:2745:146976:18:18:59:562:336:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f18:B:it, increases output toX > ξX, increases Neutral and Knightian wealth toˆWN=1ξWN> WN
58:2746:147060:18:18:59:563:318:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:andˆWK=1ξWK> WK, increasesrand decreasesrK. After the Poisson event, it leaves output
58:2747:147145:18:18:59:563:300:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:and interest rates unchanged. These imply that: Neutrals that are already born at the time of the
58:2748:147242:18:18:59:563:282:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:increase in the inflation target are strictly better off (their wealth jumps at impact and the rates of
58:2749:147345:18:18:59:563:264:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:return on their wealth is unchanged going forward); Neutrals that are born after the increase in the
58:2750:147445:18:18:59:563:246:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:inflation target but before the Poisson event are strictly better off (their income when newborn is
58:2751:147544:18:18:59:563:228:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:higher and the rates of return on their wealth is unchanged); Neutrals and Knightians that are born
58:2752:147643:18:18:59:563:210:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:after the increase in the inflation target and the Poisson event are as well off (their income when
58:2753:147742:18:18:59:563:192:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:newborn is identical and the rates of return on their wealth is unchanged); however Knightians that
58:2754:147841:18:18:59:563:174:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:are already born at the time of the increase of the inflation target are strictly worse off (their initial
58:2755:147947:18:18:59:563:156:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:wealth is unchanged but the rate of return on their wealth is lower); and Knightians that are born
58:2756:148045:18:16:69:563:138:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f7:F:39Withλ+>0 orλ−>0,rnow decreases to ˆr < rafter the public debt issuance, so that we can no longer
58:2757:148143:16:12:59:563:122:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:conclude that the public debt issuance generates a Pareto improvement through the reasoning above.  It clearly
58:2758:148253:12:12:59:563:110:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:makes Knightians better off , it will benefit some Neutrals, but it might make some Neutrals worse off. The welfare
58:2759:148368:12:11:59:563:98:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:properties of public debt issuances then depend on the relative weighting of gains and losses. For example, we can

59:2799:150431:45:31:59:301:370:14:g_d0_f9:14:g_d0_f9:C:A.5  Bubbles and Fiscal Capacity
59:2800:150463:31:18:59:563:339:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:The very low interest rates that characterize a safety trap raises the issue of whether speculative
59:2801:150562:18:18:59:563:321:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:bubbles may emerge, and whether these can play a useful role through their wealth effect.  We
59:2802:150655:18:18:59:563:303:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:show that bubbles can indeed arise in safety traps, but that only the emergence of safe bubbles
59:2803:150750:18:18:59:563:285:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:(as opposed to risky bubbles) can stimulate economic activity. This is because only safe bubbles
59:2804:150846:18:18:59:563:267:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:alleviate the shortage of safe assets. We associate the latter to public debt, and in fact the existence
59:2805:150950:18:18:59:563:249:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:of a bubbly-region is equivalent to an expansion of the fiscal capacity of the government. We focus
59:2806:151049:18:18:59:563:231:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:on the constrained regime and on safety traps throughout in SectionsA.5.1, A.5.2, A.5.3. We briefly
59:2807:151148:18:18:59:413:213:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:consider the unconstrained regime in liquidity traps in SectionA.5.4.

59:2809:151324:15:12:59:563:180:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:are already born at the time of the increase in the inflation target or that are born after the increase in the inflation
59:2810:151445:12:12:59:563:168:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:target but before the Poisson event are not necessarily better off. With the Utilitarian welfare function considered
59:2811:151561:12:12:59:563:156:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:in the text, we can be sure that forβKlow enough andβNhigh enough, or forλ+andλ−low enough and either

65:3155:159807:0:32:59:282:756:14:g_d0_f9:14:g_d0_f9:C:A.6  Securitization Externality
65:3156:159838:32:18:59:563:724:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:In this section, we endogenize the securitization capacity of the economy.  We assume that by
65:3157:159931:18:18:59:563:706:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:investing resourcesjtXdt,a Neutral agent can increaseρ(jt) and, with it, increase the supply of
65:3158:160026:18:24:59:563:688:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:safe assets (i.e., the share of the tree’s revenue in the bad state of the world that is pledgable today).
65:3159:160132:24:18:77:563:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:We show in this extension that outside of a safety trap, the competitive equilibrium is constrained
65:3160:160231:18:17:59:563:646:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:Pareto efficient, but that in a safety trap, it is constrained inefficient (there is underprovision of
65:3161:160333:17:24:59:119:629:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:safe assets).
65:3162:160346:24:18:77:563:605:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:We trace back this inefficiency to asecuritization externality. In a safety trap, private agents
65:3163:160442:18:18:59:563:587:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:do not internalize the full social benefit of creating safe assets. More specifically, they do not take
65:3164:160545:18:18:59:563:569:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:into account the stimulative effects of these assets, which creates a role for government intervention
65:3165:160647:18:18:59:563:551:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:in the securitization market.  This argument is distinct from the comparative advantage of the
65:3166:160741:18:18:59:563:533:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:government in safe asset creation that we analyzed in Section3, but it can also be used to support
65:3167:160839:18:18:59:563:515:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:it if we associate the government extra-taxation power to the private sector’s technology to increase
65:3168:160940:18:41:59:172:497:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:safe assets (at a cost).
65:3169:160964:41:31:59:355:456:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:C:A.6.1  Securitization Externality in a Safety Trap

66:3199:162389:24:18:77:563:696:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:We now investigate the efficiency properties of the competitive equilibrium.  To do so, it is
66:3200:162482:18:18:59:563:678:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:convenient to introduce lump sum taxes that allow arbitrary redistribution within Knightians and

66:3202:162672:18:24:59:396:642:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:these taxes do not change the characterization of the equilibrium.
66:3203:162738:24:18:77:563:618:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:Consider the steady state of the competitive equilibrium with Neutral wealthWN, Knightian
66:3204:162827:18:18:59:563:600:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:wealthWK, interest ratesrandrK, and securitizationj.We focus on the constrained regime
66:3205:162913:18:17:59:563:582:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:throughout. We analyze first the case where prices are flexible. We then analyze the case with
66:3206:163007:17:18:59:563:565:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:rigid prices. In the first case, output is always at capacity. The corresponding planning problem is
66:3207:163107:18:18:59:563:547:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:easier to analyze. Moreover, as long as the natural safe real interest rate is positive, this flexible
66:3208:163209:18:18:59:563:529:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:prices planning problem is a constrained version of the rigid prices planning problem, but the
66:3209:163303:18:18:59:563:511:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:corresponding constraints are satisfied at the optimum of the latter, so that their solutions coincide.
66:3210:163406:18:24:59:455:493:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:This is no longer the case when the natural safe real interest rate is negative.
66:3211:163486:24:18:77:563:469:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:We are interested in whether it is possible to generate a Pareto improvement by controlling
66:3212:163577:18:18:59:563:451:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:securitizationjt(either through taxes or quantity restrictions) and settingit at a different level
66:3213:163675:18:18:59:563:433:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:than would occur in a competitive equilibrium without government interventions in securitization.
66:3214:163772:18:15:59:563:415:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:With the lump sum taxes mentioned above, this happens if and only if we can find processesˆWKt,
66:3215:163867:15:21:62:563:400:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:ˆWNt,ˆWt,ˆVSt,ˆVRt,ˆVt, ˆrt, ˆrKt,ˆδStand ˆtthat verify all the equilibrium equations except the first
66:3216:163970:21:18:59:563:379:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:order condition for ˆt, and such thatˆWNt≥WNtandˆWKt≥WKtfor alltand a strict inequality for
66:3217:164062:18:24:59:198:361:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:B:some positive measure oft.
